{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:10","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:10","title":"Chrome 87 Canary completely overhauls the profile setup UI","link":"https://chromeunboxed.com/?p=24936","description":"<a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chrome-user-profile-picker-canary-87\" title=\"Chrome 87 Canary completely overhauls the profile setup UI\" rel=\"nofollow\"><img width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newChromeCanary87profilePickerUI-1024x576.jpg\" class=\"webfeedsFeaturedVisual wp-post-image\" alt=\"\" loading=\"lazy\" style=\"display: block; That isn&#8217;t to say there aren&#8217;t similar behaviors between the two, but the way they handle moving from one account to another is a very different experience when sat side by side.  For Chrome OS, you sign in with a profile (Google account) and can add other Google accounts inside that system-level log in for use with apps both on the web and via Android.  That is how I operate and how most people get around on a Chromebook.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>There are inherent limitations to this approach, however, since my personal Google account is logged in on my Chromebook, my Files app accesses my personal Google Drive, not my G Suite drive that is attached to my Chrome Unboxed account.  My bookmarks and Chrome browser settings are my personal setup, not separated into personal and work.  On Windows, Mac or Linux, however, this is handled quite differently.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>On those operating systems, you log into Chrome and create user profiles.  Multiple profiles can exist on one version of Chrome and be accessed at the same time, allowing for a nice separation of work and personal setups.  You can even create desktop shortcuts to different profiles to keep things separated.  My current workflow mixes all my bookmarks together since that is the primary profile I&#8217;m logged into my Chromebook with and I honestly envy the setup Windows, Linux and Mac users get with the ability to truly separate out their work/personal accounts in Chrome.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>With all that in mind, these changes to the profile user flow won&#8217;t have any affect or be present on Chromebooks.  With Chromebooks handling the profile switching on an OS level, this all works in a very different way and the new profile setup we&#8217;re about to see simply isn&#8217;t present at all on Chromebooks and may never be.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"crp_related crp_related_block  \"><h5>more from Chrome Unboxed</h5><ul><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-account-log-in-settings-android-native/\"    target=\"_blank\"  class=\"post-10977\"><img loading=\"lazy\"  width=\"150\" height=\"150\"  src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/newLogInChromeOSunifiedFeature-150x150.jpg\" class=\"crp_thumb crp_featured\" alt=\"This new feature in Chrome OS 76 makes Android feel so much more native on Chromebooks\" title=\"This new feature in Chrome OS 76 makes Android feel so much more native on Chromebooks\" /><span class=\"crp_title\">This new feature in Chrome OS 76 makes Android feel so much more native on Chromebooks</span></a><span class=\"crp_author\">  by <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/author/robbypayne/\">Robby Payne</a></span> </li></ul><div class=\"crp_clear\"></div></div>\n\n\n<p>Now then, let&#8217;s take a look at the updated UI for adding profiles to Chrome in Windows, Linux and MacOS coming in Chrome 87 (currently in Canary) that was <a href=\"https://techdows.com/2020/08/chrome-new-profile-picker.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">spotted by Techdows.</a>  There&#8217;s not really any new functionality going on here, but the interface looks very nice and is very clear when communicating what is going on for users new to the experience of adding multiple profiles to Chrome.  Here&#8217;s the walk-through, step by step of what you&#8217;ll see in Chrome Canary after enabling the <strong>chrome://flags/#enable-new-profile-picker</strong> and <strong>chrome://flags/#enable-sign-in-profile-creation-flow</strong> flags.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"24938\" with.  Additionally, you can browse as a guest from here and choose whether you want to see this screen when Chrome is opened up each time.  You&#8217;ll also see this selector when you click your profile picture in the top-right of Chrome and choose to add a new profile.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"24939\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chrome-user-profile-picker-canary-87/newprofileui-2/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-2.png\" data-orig-size=\"1800,1200\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"newProfileUI-2\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-2-300x200.png\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-2-1024x683.png\" loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-2-1024x683.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24939\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-2-1024x683.png 1024w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-2-300x200.png 300w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-2-768x512.png 768w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-2-1536x1024.png 1536w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-2.png 1800w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><figcaption>The new add profile screen</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Next up, users are taken to the screen where they can name a new profile and, once it works, select a Google account to sync.  For now, the &#8216;Turn on sync&#8217; button doesn&#8217;t do anything, but you can log in and sync things after the initial setup.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"24940\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chrome-user-profile-picker-canary-87/newprofileui-3/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-3.png\" data-orig-size=\"1800,1200\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"newProfileUI-3\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-3-300x200.png\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-3-1024x683.png\" loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-3-1024x683.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24940\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-3-1024x683.png 1024w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-3-300x200.png 300w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-3-768x512.png 768w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-3-1536x1024.png 1536w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-3.png 1800w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>If you choose not to log in and just want a fresh, local profile to use, you can add an avatar and a nickname here.  Ideally this is where you could go ahead and choose a theme as well, but we&#8217;re not seeing that yet.  There&#8217;s a large box under the name that is useless for now, but will likely be used for something down the road.  Finally, you can go ahead and choose to create a quick desktop shortcut for this new profile from this screen.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"24941\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chrome-user-profile-picker-canary-87/newprofileui-4/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-4.png\" data-orig-size=\"1800,1200\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"newProfileUI-4\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-4-300x200.png\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-4-1024x683.png\" loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-4-1024x683.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24941\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-4-1024x683.png 1024w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-4-300x200.png 300w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-4-768x512.png 768w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-4-1536x1024.png 1536w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/newProfileUI-4.png 1800w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><figcaption>Profile made, ready to log in</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Finally, you get to this colorful screen where you can get started or choose to log in and sync an existing Google account.  Once synced up, all you usual Chrome settings and bookmarks will come along for the ride and this local profile will be tied to you cloud data.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Overall, the user flow update looks nice and is very clear in displaying and conveying the profile setup process.  I&#8217;m not sure how many users take advantage of this feature in Chrome, but if you are currently not on a Chromebook and using Chrome, I&#8217;d highly recommend getting started with profiles if you leverage multiple Google accounts.  It&#8217;s a very clean way to stay productive and keep you work from bleeding into you persona online time.  Look for these new UI updates to hit sometime late in 2020 when Chrome 87 is scheduled to roll out.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"BuyButton\" rel=\"noopener data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/google-meet-nod-hand-raise-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>Class is in session for thousands of students and many will be learning remotely using tools such as Google Classroom and Google Meet. Since the onset of the pandemic that sent so many of us into our homes, Google Meet, Zoom and other video conferencing platforms have experienced explosive growth and as a result, have been inclined to beef up features in a response to the growing growing trend of remote work and learning. While Zoom has become the platform for millions of users, Google too has risen to the challenge with new features and wider availability of video conferencing platform that was once exclusive to GSuite accounts. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Google Meet makes perfect sense for the countless institutions that already use Google Classroom and manage accounts and devices with GSuite&#8217;s Admin Console. However, despite the recent upgrades and improvements to Google Meet, there are a few attributes that are still lacking from Google&#8217;s robust video chat. In late June, Google announced that GSuite Education accounts would eventually add the ability for participants to use the &#8220;raise&#8221; hand&#8221; feature which allows teachers to maintain order in the virtual classroom. This feature is set to come along with other updates such as virtual whiteboards for collaboration and attendance tracking but they aren&#8217;t slated to arrive until October. <strong>So, what do you do in the mean time? </strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you have a friendly IT admin who&#8217;s willing to help you out, there are some third-party tools to help you get the most out of you Google Meet virtual classroom. We&#8217;ve talked about some of these in the past but when the pandemic started, few of us expected that it would have the long-term effects that would potentially extend into 2021. So, we&#8217;re going to highlight three Chrome extensions that can help you manage your Google Meet video chats and hopefully, get the most out of your virtual school day. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Nod</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>I can tell you from my daughter&#8217;s first day of online learning, teachers do not have it easy when it comes to managing a virtual room full of second graders. When you&#8217;re in-person, it&#8217;s much easier to directly address an individual student and handle feedback, in general. When you have 30+ students in a Google Meet chat, getting everyone to mute their mics and interact via chat or simply wave at the camera to get the teacher&#8217;s attention is a massive undertaking. It creates a bit of a chaotic environment and that takes away from the entire learning experience. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed-youtube aligncenter wp-block-embed is-type-video is-provider-youtube wp-embed-aspect-16-9 wp-has-aspect-ratio\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\n<iframe title=\"Nod - Reactions for Google Meet\" width=\"500\" height=\"281\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/KpqifxNXrLA?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n</div></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>While you&#8217;re waiting for Google to add the hand-raise feature to Meet, you can ask your IT admin to add this &#8220;handy&#8221; extension to your approved list and even push it to school-owned devices and accounts. Nod-Reactions for Google Meet gives every user the ability to grab the teacher&#8217;s attention with a silent raise of a digital hand. In addition to keeping order with hand raises, Nod offers a handful of emoji responses that are perfect for students to let their teacher know that they are on pace with the current lesson. Visual feedback is very important when you&#8217;re meeting online and Nod offers a simple and free way to do just that with minimal disruption to the learning environment. If you are using Google Meet without a GSuite account, you can use Nod right now. If you&#8217;re interested in getting for your classroom, contact your IT department and ask them to help you get it set up for you and your students. Find it in the Chrome Web Store below. </p>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://chrome.google.com/webstore/detail/nod-reactions-for-google/oikgofeboedgfkaacpfepbfmgdalabej?hl=en\" class=\"BuyButton\" target=\"_blank\">Nod &#8211; Reactions for Google Meet</a></p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Google Meet Attendance</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Another feature that Google has promised is on the way for Meet is the ability for teachers to take attendance digitally right in the video chat. This will be a powerful tool when it finally arrives as it will save teachers hours upon hours of precious time throughout the school year. Thankfully, teachers are resourceful and many of them take it upon themselves to find solutions instead of waiting on someone else to do it. I found a couple of extensions that take on the task of attendance rosters in Google Meet but one, in particular, stood out because it&#8217;s simple, does exactly what you want it to and gets out of the way when you&#8217;re not using it. </p>\n\n\n<div class=\"crp_related crp_related_block  \"><h5>more from Chrome Unboxed</h5><ul><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/zoom-responds-security-fixes-industry-standard-zoombombing-password-waiting-room/\"    target=\"_blank\"  class=\"post-16644\"><img loading=\"lazy\"  width=\"150\" height=\"150\"  src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Zoom-White-150x150.jpg\" class=\"crp_thumb crp_featured\" alt=\"Zoom&#039;s response to its own flaws should set the industry standard\" title=\"Zoom&#039;s response to its own flaws should set the industry standard\" /><span class=\"crp_title\">Zoom&#8217;s response to its own flaws should set the industry standard</span></a><span class=\"crp_author\">  by <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/author/gabe/\">Gabriel Brangers</a></span> </li></ul><div class=\"crp_clear\"></div></div>\n\n\n<p>Google Meet Attendance was created by a Math and Computer teacher out of Ontario. Mr. Caughey developed the Chrome extension for the very same reason many of you landed on this article. <strong>Attendance</strong>. However, his free extension does even more that just punch the attendance roster. Teachers can create and save multiple class lists and when students join Meet, their attendance is registered. Not only that, the extension will tell you how long each student was in the meeting and their is support for eight languages with more on the way. The reports are saved in a neat, HTML form for teachers to use as needed. The developer does emphasize that the extension collects NO data so it&#8217;s safe for your students to use and you can find that policy and more on the Git page <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://github.com/al-caughey/Google-Meet-Attendance\" target=\"_blank\">here</a>. You can download the Google Meet Attendance extension from the Web Store at the link below but don&#8217;t forget to get with you IT admin to get it enabled. </p>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://chrome.google.com/webstore/detail/google-meet-attendance/fkdjflnaggakjamjkmimcofefhppfljd/related?hl=en\" class=\"BuyButton\" target=\"_blank\">Google Meet Attendance</a></p>\n\n\n\n<p>I don&#8217;t know about you, but this fine gentleman up in Canada deserves some major accolades. Not only has he been preparing for a school year of remote learning and working, he has taken the time and energy to invest in his fellow educators. Not only that, he&#8217;s doing it absolutely free and is very active on Facebook ready to take input, feedback and suggestions to improve an already amazing Chrome Extension and classroom tool. If you grab this extension and find it handy or maybe you just want to support someone who invests in the future our children, you can donate to this teacher/developer. You can find the link on the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.facebook.com/GoogleMeetAttendance/\" target=\"_blank\">Extension&#8217;s Facebook page</a> and on the Chrome Web Store in the description. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Google Meet Push To Talk</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Tired of yelling at your students and trying to get them to mute their mics? Make them work to chat with this handy little extension that adds a &#8220;CB radio&#8221; aspect to your video meetings. Google Meet Push to Talk does exactly what the name clearly states. With this extension installed, you have everyone in your meeting mute their mics by default. Then, if you want to speak, you just have to press the space bar. Just like two way radios when we were kids. This won&#8217;t take the place of hand raising or reactions but it&#8217;s a great way to keep the chatter at a minimum and eliminate everyone talking at once. </p>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://chrome.google.com/webstore/detail/google-meet-push-to-talk/pgpidfocdapogajplhjofamgeboonmmj?hl=en-US\" class=\"BuyButton\" target=\"_blank\">Google Meet Push To Talk</a></p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Update</strong>: <em>I received an email from the CIO of a large school district who pointed out some very useful information about extensions of this nature. While they are very helpful tools, these extensions are not published or supported by Google. These are third-party tools and many of them are developed by teachers wanting to fill a gap in technology. Updates to Google Meet can often times break extensions like these when updates are pushed that cause conflicts that the developers can not foresee. If you are using these extensions and Meet is having issues, you will want to disable the third-party extensions before taking further troubleshooting steps. </em></p>\n\n\n\n<div them.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>USB 4.0 is on the way for Chromebooks</h2>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25254\" 4.0</a> and the potential for it hitting a next-gen Chromebook already, but I&#8217;ll quickly recap why its a big deal.  For one, USB 4.0 will unify USB under one connector: USB Type C.  If it utilizing USB 4.0, it will have the Type C connector.  <strong>No more confusion there.</strong>  Additionally, we&#8217;re looking at 40GB/s transfer speeds, Thunderbolt 3, PD (power deliver for fast charging standards) and backwards compatibility with older USB 3.2 and USB 2.0 protocols.  This is a next-gen connectivity standard we will all come to expect as we move into 2021, so I&#8217;m glad to see &#8216;Halvor&#8217; will come equipped with it.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Thunderbolt is finally coming to Chromebooks, too</h2>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-thunderbolt-3-support-chrome-os/\" target=\"_blank\">We&#8217;ve talked about Thunderbolt support for Chromebooks</a> on multiple occasions and, honestly, we thought we&#8217;d eventually see it hit a &#8216;Hatch&#8217;-based Chromebook like the Samsung Galaxy Chromebook or Acer Spin 713, but there&#8217;s been no real movement on that front with the current generation of Chromebooks.  Tiger Lake Chromebooks based on the &#8216;Volteer&#8217; baseboard, on the other hand, look set to deliver the benefits of Thunderbolt to Chrome OS and &#8216;Halvor&#8217; definitely looks to be getting in on the action.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The benefits?  Thunderbolt greatly increases data transfer speeds for things like external GPUs and SSDs, but is also plays a very important role in giving Chromebooks a far greater ability to leverage multiple external displays at once.  While not a tool every user is after right now, the additional headroom is definitely welcome on higher-end Chromebooks from a productivity standpoint and, with the addition of both USB 4.0 and Thunderbolt, it appears Google&#8217;s next Chromebook won&#8217;t be at a loss for external data transfer prowess.</p>\n\n\n\n<img href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-80-virtual-desktops-4-finger-gesture-switch-stable-no-flags/\" target=\"_blank\">rolled-out in fullness in March of this year.</a>  Since that time, there&#8217;s not been a whole lot of development on this highly-useful feature apart from <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-83-brings-persistent-virtual-desks/\" target=\"_blank\">the ability to rename your desks</a> and, honestly, I&#8217;m OK with that.  The feature has been so solid and great to use that it has become a regular part of my daily workflow and one I have a hard time imagining living without.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>It looks like a solid upgrade will be coming to Virtual Desks via a small-but-helpful change for people that like to use these desks as a legitimate productivity tool.  <a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2376418\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">According to this commit from the Chromium Repositories,</a> Virtual Desks are getting an upgrade in the speed department that will allow quick moves between all four desks to happen with much higher rates of speed.  </p>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p>desks: Allow multiple keyboard press to switch desks quickly. </p><p>Second CL to allow chaining keyboard shortcuts. </p><p>Follow up to <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://crrev.com/c/2354798\" target=\"_blank\">crrev.com/c/2354798</a> which allows RootWindowDeskSwitch to handle more than two screenshots. This CL fills it out by handling taking third and fourth screenshots and placing them on the animation layer to get a nice smooth continuous animation. Tests in a follow up.</p><cite><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2376418\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">via the Chromium Gerrit</a></cite></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<p>As it stands right now, if you use the keyboard shortcut to move through your open desks <strong>( SEARCH + [ or ] )</strong>, you&#8217;ll notice you can only move to the next desk once the desk you just jumped to slides fully into view.  Hit that shortcut key before the animation finishes and nothing happens.  What this means is jumping from desk 1 to desk 4 can take a few seconds at best and a tad longer at worst.  </p>\n\n\n\n<p>If, like me, you use Virtual Desks on a regular basis, this can add up to a lot of wasted time moving through your open desks.  I tend to put the same stuff on my desks every day, so I always know that my music player and related media is always on my 4th desk, for instance, and moving to that desk from my 1st desk (where my primary stuff lives) takes a second or two no matter how I go about doing it.  Not a huge headache, but I can easily see where quicker transitions could go a long way.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This upcoming change should allow users to move from desk to desk with much less time between animations, meaning if you are on desk 1 and need to skip right to desk 4, you can hit that keyboard shortcut 3 times in succession and land right on the desk you need without waiting for animations to load each time.  For users that are invested in using Virtual Desks on their Chromebook, this tiny change could go a long way towards saving us all quite a bit of time.  We&#8217;ll be on the lookout for this change to be merged and will give it a try in the Canary Channel as soon as we see it arrive.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" 16:50:10","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:10","title":"Hands-On: USI pens for Chromebooks are finally arriving and they are awesome [VIDEO]","link":"https://chromeunboxed.com/?p=25054","description":"<a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/usi-stylus-pen-chromebook-hands-on\" title=\"Hands-On: USI pens for Chromebooks are finally arriving and they are awesome [VIDEO]\" rel=\"nofollow\"><img width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/USIpenChromebook-1024x576.jpg\" class=\"webfeedsFeaturedVisual wp-post-image\" alt=\"\" loading=\"lazy\" style=\"display: block; margin: auto; margin-bottom: 10px;max-width: 100%;\" link_thumbnail=\"1\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/USIpenChromebook-1024x576.jpg 1024w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/USIpenChromebook-300x169.jpg 300w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/USIpenChromebook.jpg 2000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" data-attachment-id=\"25057\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/usi-stylus-pen-chromebook-hands-on/usipenchromebook/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/USIpenChromebook.jpg\" data-orig-size=\"2000,1125\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;4&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;ILCE-6000&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;1601219457&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;50&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;640&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0.00625&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;1&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"USIpenChromebook\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/USIpenChromebook-300x169.jpg\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/USIpenChromebook-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p><strong>The story of USI pens is a long one.</strong>  In fact, the entire USI (universal stylus initiative) platform dates all the way back to 2015.  In a similar manner to unifying ports under one, universal standard (USB), USI aims to wrangle all the differing, proprietary digital pen technologies into one, unified standard.  That&#8217;s a big undertaking for any organization and part of the reason why after 5 years, we&#8217;re just now getting to the point where we have quite a few devices that can leverage the tech.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/rise-of-the-universal-stylus-usi-emerges-in-upcoming-chromebook-bloog/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">We began tracking USI input on upcoming Chromebooks all the way back in May of 2019</a> and knew that, eventually, we&#8217;d begin seeing some Chromebooks launch with it on board.  What we didn&#8217;t realize is the fact that most Chromebooks launching in 2020 would come equipped with USI capability if they chose to go with pen support.  While Samsung is a participant in the USI movement, they bucked the trend and shipped the Galaxy Chromebook very early in 2020 with their own internal stylus tech (EMR-based).  Apart from them, however, all Chromebooks launched this year that have digital pen support are based on USI.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>The ASUS Flip C436, HP x360 14c, HP x360 12b, Lenovo Flex 5, Lenovo Duet, Lenovo 10e, and Acer Spin 713</strong> are all big releases for 2020 that lean on the USI tech to offer users a pen experience.  <strong>The problem?</strong>  Up to this point, there have simply been no pens available for anyone to go and buy.  Pair that up with the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/the-chrome-cast-episode-69-interview-john-maletis-chrome-os-head-ux/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"19901\" target=\"_blank\">massive Chromebook growth we&#8217;ve seen across the board in 2020</a> and you have a large audience hungry for pens that have simply been non-existent up to this point.  It&#8217;s been a bit of bad timing, for sure, but it finally seems we&#8217;re on the other side of the issue as <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/certified-usi-universal-stylus-initiative-available-iplume-chromebook-compatible\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25015\" target=\"_blank\">3rd-party USI pens have begun to show up here and there,</a> signaling an end to the USI pen drought.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed-youtube aligncenter wp-block-embed is-type-video is-provider-youtube wp-embed-aspect-16-9 wp-has-aspect-ratio\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\n<iframe title=\"Hands-On: USI Pens for Chromebooks are Finally Arriving\" width=\"500\" height=\"281\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/0x-ekbCOOIg?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n</div></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Testing one of many USI pens</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We&#8217;ve recently had the opportunity to have a chat with the Chairman of USI &#8211; Peter Mueller &#8211; and we are excited about having him on the podcast this week, but as a part of that chat came the chance to finally get our hands on a few working, real-world USI pens being made by 3rd-party ODMs.  Specifically, the pen we have in the office is made by Waltop for a variety of resellers and is the <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/certified-usi-universal-stylus-initiative-available-iplume-chromebook-compatible\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25015\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">exact same pen we came across recently on Amazon being sold and branded as iPlume.</a></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Getting this pen in the office allowed us to finally test a working, production-level USI pen on a few Chromebooks we have around and, <strong>you know what?  These pens are legit.</strong>  Not only does the all-aluminum casing feel premium, the input lag is fantastic (even on the slowest USI Chromebook in the Lenovo Duet), the pressure sensitivity is responsive, and the feel of the pen on the screen is satisfying as well.  There was no need to pair the pen up or go through any setup processes: it simply jumped between all the USI-compatible Chromebooks we have around without even a hiccup.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"crp_related crp_related_block  \"><h5>more from Chrome Unboxed</h5><ul><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-chromebook-zork-usi-stylus-pen-internal-charge/\"    target=\"_blank\"  class=\"post-19809\"><img loading=\"lazy\"  width=\"150\" height=\"150\"  src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/AMDchromebooksCES2020-150x150.jpg\" class=\"crp_thumb crp_featured\" alt=\"Upcoming AMD-powered Chromebooks will internally stow and charge a USI stylus\" title=\"Upcoming AMD-powered Chromebooks will internally stow and charge a USI stylus\" /><span class=\"crp_title\">Upcoming AMD-powered Chromebooks will internally stow and charge a USI stylus</span></a><span class=\"crp_author\">  by <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/author/robbypayne/\">Robby Payne</a></span> </li></ul><div class=\"crp_clear\"></div></div>\n\n\n<p>This pen &#8211; and the others like it that are finally coming to market &#8211; is as good as any first-party pen on any Chromebook I&#8217;ve tested, and <strong>I&#8217;m so thrilled to be able to say that.</strong>  Our only USI pen experience has been with a pre-production HP pen that, frankly, hasn&#8217;t been great.  Up to this point, we were honestly unsure if the fault was with the pen or with the USI standard, but we can confidently tell you that USI is for real and pens that are built correctly work like a charm on any Chromebook you use them with.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>I hope you have a moment to watch the video we made on this because I can only tell you so much: watching brings it to life.  <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://universalstylus.org/members/\" target=\"_blank\">With so many big names on board with the USI pen efforts,</a> we can realistically see a near-term future when there are tons of USI pens to choose from and tons of laptops that utilize the universally-adopted tech.  It&#8217;s one thing to have a standard that just works; <strong>it&#8217;s a much bigger deal to have a universal standard that works well and is actually great to use in practice.</strong>  If you&#8217;ve purchased a Chromebook this year with the hopes of choosing the pen that you want for it, the time is finally arriving where that is going to be an option, and the end result will be a fantastic inking experience for everyone.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"BuyButton\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Shop Best Chromebooks of 2020 So Far on data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ctl-nl81-14-chromebook-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>Chromebooks are scarce. If you&#8217;ve looked around the web in an attempt to find a decent device at a price that doesn&#8217;t induce a stroke, you probably know exactly what I&#8217;m talking about. As of this morning, Best Buy had less than six Chromebook models in stock and three of those were variants of the Pixelbook Go. While most manufacturers are working diligently to get new models into the market, it looks like late fall is going to be the earliest we see most devices back in stock on a regular basis. CTL has been at the mercy of high demand and short supply like everyone else but that hasn&#8217;t stopped the Oregon-base Chromebook maker from getting some new products in the pipeline.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In a company first, CTL has debuted two 14&#8243; Chromebooks and these devices are looking to shake up the mid-range Chrome OS market thanks to some impressive specs with a very palatable price tag. For starters, CTL&#8217;s base model 14&#8243; Chromebook comes out of the gate with a Full HD display which is not the norm when we&#8217;re talking EDU devices. Both devices feature Intel Gemini Lake-R CPUs that boasts processing power that&#8217;s more than ample for the majority of users. I&#8217;m not just talking about your middle school student, either. We&#8217;ll talk a little more about that in a second. For now, let&#8217;s take a look at the new Chromebooks from CTL. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>CTL Chromebook NL81</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The entry-level 14&#8243; Chromebook NL81 features a Full HD anti-glare panel which should make for a great workspace. It is powered by the dual-core Intel Gemini Lake-R N4020 which we have seen in a handful of devices as of late. As you can see in <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/lenovo-chromebook-ideapad-3-review-cheap-good-review/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"19638\" target=\"_blank\">our review of the Lenovo Chromebook 3</a>, this small core CPU is a workhorse and will chew threw anything the average user can throw at it. This model is paired with 4GB of RAM and 32GB of storage. It&#8217;s a bit scant on that end but let&#8217;s remember, this is and EDU device. 4GB is still enough when used in conjunction with a decent processor. For the storage, you do get a MicroSD card slot and of course, you have Google Drive right there in your files app. Moving on. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>As with all CTL Chromebooks, this model features its own share of rugged specifications. The keyboard is spill-resistant and the keys are anti-peel. We&#8217;ll have to get our hands on the NL81 to see just how tough it is but CTL does state that it is drop-tested with an IP rating and a non-slip design. Oh yeah, it also has Bluetooth 5 and Gigabit Wi-Fi. It&#8217;s not quite a zippy as Wi-Fi 6 but I doubt you&#8217;ll notice. Here&#8217;s a closer look at the CTL Chromebook NL81: </p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><strong>Chrome OS</strong></li><li><strong>Processor</strong>: Intel Gemini Lake R N4020</li><li><strong>RAM:</strong>&#160;4GB LPDDR4</li><li><strong>Storage:</strong>&#160;32GB eMMC</li><li><strong>Camera:</strong>&#160;HD 720P with LED indicator</li><li><strong>GPU:</strong>&#160;Intel® UMA GLK-R&#160;Integrated Graphics</li><li><strong>Display:</strong>&#160;16:9 14&#8243; 1920 X 1080p FHD LED Anti-Glare</li><li><strong>Ports:&#160;</strong>2x USB 3.0, 2x USB-C with PD function, 2-in-1 SD/MMC Card Reader, Audio Combo Jack</li><li><strong>Audio:&#160;</strong>Single Digital Microphone</li><li><strong>WLAN</strong>:&#160;WL/BT 802.11ABGN/AC 9560.NGWG.NV, Intel® 9560 Wireless, MU-MIMO support</li><li><strong>AUE June 2026</strong></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>Here&#8217;s the best part of this device. It is available for pre-order for the discounted price of $279. The MSRP will eventually be $349 but I&#8217;d argue that you&#8217;d be hard-pressed to find another device, available or not, that carries this kind of price tag and offers this much in the way of specs. For reference, Acer&#8217;s Chromebook 314 has a 1366&#215;768 panel, the older N4000 CPU, and retails for $249. You may not think it would make a big difference but believe me, your eyes will appreciate having a FullHD panel and the performance boost of the N4020 is worth the extra few bucks, in my opinion. The Chromebook NL81 won&#8217;t ship until Nov/Dec but pre-orders are up and you will snag that discount if you reserve now. I know that doesn&#8217;t help if you need a Chromebook right now but this will be a great option for schools looking to boost their laptop fleets as we round out 2020. </p>\n\n\n\n<p><a /></figure></li></ul></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>CTL Chromebook NL81T</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>CTL&#8217;s second model builds on the NL81 with the addition of a FullHD touch display and the Pentium N5030 CPU. This processor puts up Octane scores over 21,000 in devices that we have tested and this Chromebook gets the added boost of 8GB of RAM and 64GB of storage. It features the same rugged specs and generous port selection. Acer&#8217;s comparable model will retail for $429 but CTL is listing the NL81T for only $379 and you&#8217;re getting the exact same performance on top of the durability that CTL is known for in its Chromebooks. Pre-orders are open and the Chromebook NL81T will ship in late November or early December. We&#8217;ll get these in the office ASAP and let you know if the CTL NL81 will be the Chromebook to beat in this segment. </p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><strong>Chrome eMMC</li><li><strong>Camera:</strong>&#160;HD 720P with LED indicator</li><li><strong>GPU:</strong>&#160;Intel® UMA GLK-R&#160;Integrated Graphics</li><li><strong>Display:</strong>&#160;16:9 14&#8243; 1920 X 1080p 10-point capacitive touch</li><li><strong>Ports:&#160;</strong>2x USB 3.0, 2x USB-C with PD function, 2-in-1 SD/MMC Card Reader</li><li><strong>Audio:&#160;</strong>Dual microphone, 1x Audio Combo Jack</li><li><strong>WLAN</strong>:&#160;WL/BT 802.11ABGN/AC 9560.NGWG.NV, Intel® 9560 Wireless, MU-MIMO support</li><li><strong>AUE June 2026</strong></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p><a data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/GoogleChromebookDevelopmentBoards-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>I remember a day when finding one new Chromebook development board was cause for celebration and excitement.  I remember the thrill of the hunt and the days following a new find, filled with digging and questions around what this new Chromebook would end up becoming.  Those were simpler days and we always knew there would come a time when the number of Chromebooks in development would make it nearly impossible to keep tabs on them all.  <strong>We&#8217;re in that future, now, and the sheer volume of new Chromebooks in development is simply unprecedented.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>We have a post that I&#8217;d recommend you bookmark if you like keeping up with this kind of thing.  As we find new devices in development, <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-upcoming-development-boards-devices-chrome-os/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"18348\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">we add them to that single post</a> and try to keep it as updated as possible.  From that single page, you can see all the devices we are keeping an eye on and get a better feel for the absolute mess of Chromebooks that are coming to market in the coming months.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>For this post, however, I want to shine a light on a few newer devices we&#8217;ve come across while scouring the Chromium Repositories in search of new features and other Chrome OS goodies.  Like other devices we come across, we know very little about these Chromebooks apart from what baseboard they are built on at this point.  For some of them, details will end up surfacing over time and for others, we won&#8217;t know any other finer points until the device shows up in our office.  It&#8217;s just the way of things and when compared to only having a new board here or there to talk about, I&#8217;d rather be in the midst of this current deluge.  <strong>With that, let&#8217;s look at what&#8217;s new.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<h2>New &#8216;Volteer&#8217; Chromebooks</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The current bell of the ball is &#8216;Volteer&#8217; and the 11th-gen Tiger Lake chips devices built on this baseboard will contain.  These devices will have the option of USB 4.0, Thunderbolt, Intel&#8217;s new Xe GPU, and enhanced performance/battery life.  Just like the current &#8216;Hatch&#8217; Chromebooks we&#8217;ve watched launch in 2020 (Samsung Galaxy Chromebook, Acer Chromebook Spin 713, etc.), &#8216;Volteer&#8217; Chromebooks may show up late in 2020 and will dominate the release cycles in 2021.  Here are the new ones:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2297074\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Lingcod&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2309512\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Lindar&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2327361\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Todor&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2321809\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Eldrid&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h2>New &#8216;Zork&#8217; Chromebooks</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The other big development category right now is the group of devices based on &#8216;Zork&#8217;.  These Chromebooks will be distinctive in the fact that they possess flagship-level AMD APUs that combine powerful AMD chips with Ryzen GPUs.  While we&#8217;ve had a handful of AMD A4 and A6 Chromebooks, the processors inside were budget and meant for affordable devices.  These &#8216;Zork&#8217; boards are meant for bigger, better things and we&#8217;re very excited to see them begin to arrive as the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/steam-games-chrome-os-chromebooks-web-install-app-manager\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25260\" target=\"_blank\">movement on Steam gaming for Chromebooks is accelerating.</a>  Here are the newest additions:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2306889\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Dirinboz&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2214445\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Woomax&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h2>New &#8216;Kukui&#8217; Chromebooks</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>&#8216;Kukui&#8217; Chromebooks bring things back to 2020 development and are responsible for devices like the Lenovo Chromebook Duet and 10e.  Those devices only scratch the surface of what we&#8217;re expecting to see in the affordable Chromebook category from this baseboard.  There are many &#8216;Kukui&#8217; boards that have been in the works for quite some time and we&#8217;re adding a few more to the mix:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2319495\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Willow&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2319498\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Burnet&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2319499\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Esche&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h2>New &#8216;Dedede&#8217; Chromebooks</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Finally, our &#8216;Dedede&#8217; family is based on the upcoming Jasper Lake chip set from Intel.  These new chips may not be as flashy as the Tiger Lake chips that are pushing flagship machines, but their smaller process (10nm) and increased speed and graphics will make them awesome chips for mid-range Chromebooks.  The current crop of Gemini Lake Chromebooks are impressive in their battery life and performance at low prices, so we&#8217;d expect even better cost/performance ratios with Jasper Lake when they arrive.  Here are the new additions:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/overlays/chromiumos-overlay/+/2223557\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Drawcia&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2227769\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Boten&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2301561\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Madoo&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>For now, that is all we&#8217;ve found to add to the <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-upcoming-development-boards-devices-chrome-os/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"18348\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">ongoing list of tracked, upcoming Chromebooks.</a>  We&#8217;re always on the hunt for more and we fully expect to see more AMD and Intel Tiger Lake devices pop up for the next few months.  It&#8217;s an exciting time to be a Chromebook fan and we cannot wait to see the fruits of all this labor by the Chrome OS team. data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"change-your-password-chromebook\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/change-your-password-chromebook-300x180.jpg\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/change-your-password-chromebook.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>I will admit, I do not change my password as frequently as I probably should. That said, there are a number of reasons why one would want to update, change, or reset a Chromebook password. Thankfully, your Chromebook password is tied directly to your Google account and the credentials are one and the same. Perhaps you&#8217;re like millions of users whose email accounts have fallen victim to an unfortunate data breach. Maybe you&#8217;re like me and it&#8217;s just time to update your password for the sake of security. In another, all too familiar scenario, you may have lost or forgotten your account password and you need to reset it to regain access to your Google services. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Today, we&#8217;re going to take a look at the proper methods to change and/or reset your Google password depending on your specific situation. We&#8217;ll start with the easiest scenario and then, move on to the more sticky implementations of changing your password. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you simply want to change your login password for your Chromebook, you just have to update the password associated with the Google account that you use to log in. This is best done from the Chromebook you use regularly. This method takes presumes that you know your current Google password. To begin, open up a New Tab Page on your Chromebook. If you have a custom New Tab Page, you can just go to Google or any of your connected Google services such as Gmail or Google Drive. At the top-right corner, you should see your profile picture. Click the photo and select &#8220;Manage your Google account.&#8221; It will be the one directly below your photo, not the one at the bottom of the dropdown. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gallery columns-1 is-cropped\"><ul 1024px\" /></a></figure></li></ul></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>If you have multiple accounts logged into your device, double-check to make sure that you are headed to the account you wish to update. You can actually get to this page faster by heading to your personal Google activity URL. Just click this link. <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://myaccount.google.com/\" target=\"_blank\">My Google Account</a>. Pretty cool, huh? Next, you will need to find the password settings. On the left-hand menu, click &#8220;Security&#8221; and the second item in the list should say &#8220;Signing in to Google.&#8221; The top line says &#8220;password&#8221; and that&#8217;s the one you want to click in order to update your password. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gallery columns-1 is-cropped\"><ul data-carousel-extra='{\"blog_id\":1,\"permalink\":\"https:\\/\\/chromeunboxed.com\\/how-to-reset-the-password-on-your-chromebook-the-right-way\\/\"}' class=\"blocks-gallery-grid\"><li 100vw, 779px\" /></a></figure></li><li class=\"blocks-gallery-item\"><figure><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-6.png\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25150\" 100vw, 887px\" /></a></figure></li></ul></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You will now be prompted to enter your current password before you can access the security settings. Now you can set your new Google password. <em><strong>Note</strong>: This will require you to sign in with the new password on any device that uses your Google account. That means your phone, PCs that you use with Chrome, and any smart devices that are linked to your Google account may need to be updated with the new password.</em> Once you&#8217;ve saved your new password, there is one last step. Close your tabs and any apps you may have open. Now, power down the Chromebook. This will update the TPM with the new password and you&#8217;re all set. If you&#8217;re like us, you might have more than one Chromebook around the house. Now would be a good time to go ahead and update the password on those devices. To do this, you will need to log into the other devices with the old password. Once you&#8217;ve done that, Chrome OS should prompt you to update your credentials and sign in again. It&#8217;s best to do this sooner than later so you don&#8217;t forget your old password and lock yourself out of a device. That leads us to the next scenario that would have you reset your password. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Lost or forgotten</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>In the event you forget your Google password, I have good news and bad news. In most cases, you can reset the password to your Google account. Unfortunately, your Chrome OS device can only be accessed with the password that you have forgotten. This is why it is imperative that you keep important data and <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/backup-and-restore-your-chromebooks-linux-setup/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25047\" target=\"_blank\">files backed up</a> to your Google Drive account, external storage, or some other form of off-device storage. Most Android app data is synced to your Google Play account so that&#8217;s not a real concern but any saved files from the web, documents, applications (Android or Linux) or anything else will be lost forever if it is only saved locally on your device and you have lost your password. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you have data saved that you absolutely do not wish to lose, make sure you have a sure-fire way to remember your password. That said, there are some instances where you simply can&#8217;t remember your password. If that is the case, logging back into your Chromebook will require a powerwash. This process will completely erase any data on the device. That includes any other accounts that may be logged into the Chromebook. As you can see, you want to avoid this path unless you have absolutely no other alternative. To get started, you will need access to a PC or even the guest mode on a Chromebook. Navigate to the Google login page and enter the email for the password you need to reset. You can find that page <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://accounts.google.com/signin\" target=\"_blank\">here</a>.  Beneath the password field, click the &#8220;forgot password&#8221; link. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25165\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/how-to-reset-the-password-on-your-chromebook-the-right-way/google-forgot-password/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password.jpg\" data-orig-size=\"1137,616\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"google-forgot-password\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-300x163.jpg\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-1024x555.jpg\" loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"555\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-1024x555.jpg\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25165\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-1024x555.jpg 1024w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-300x163.jpg 300w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-768x416.jpg 768w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password.jpg 1137w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You will be prompted to try the last password that you can remember for the account. If you want to try an old password, go ahead. You may luck out and the process will continue. If you can&#8217;t think of one, select &#8220;try another way&#8221; and see what options you have. If you have a recovery email, you will be able to send a link to the other email that will let you reset your password. If you have set up 2FA with your Android device, you can choose to verify it with your phone. You will receive a notification on your mobile device asking for confirmation. Hit yes on your phone and your browser should forward you to the page where you can set up your new password. Save that and close your browser. This would be a good time to point out that your Google Account offers a number of ways to back up and recover your account. You should have that setup. Just sayin&#8217;.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, it&#8217;s time to turn to your locked Chromebook. If you&#8217;re logged into your Chromebook, you can powerwash from the settings menu. Sadly, you can&#8217;t log in. If you could, you probably wouldn&#8217;t be reading this. Instead, we&#8217;ll have to do some keyboard gymnastics to reset your device. <strong>Remember, this will delete all data on your device. It will be reset to factory settings.</strong> To reset your device, make sure all users are logged out. from the sign-in screen, press the keys <strong>CTRL+SHIFT+ALT+R</strong>. The powerwash screen will pop up and prompt you to confirm the reset. The device will then restart on go through the reset process. Once it is finished, you will be able to log in with your Google Account and newly updated password. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you have a managed device from work or school, these methods do not necessarily work. You will need to contact your IT Admin to see what steps you will need to take in order to reset or recover your password. We will cover those various methods at another time. For now, I hope this helps get you back up and running sooner than later. </p>\n","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 01 Sep 2020 18:48:20 +0000","feedId":13345,"bgimg":"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/change-your-password-chromebook.jpg","linkMd5":"b15a25383b14859a76a604113ecf28a9","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn26@2020_3/2020/09/05/08-50-11-628_c9dd47830af22981.webp","destWidth":1024,"destHeight":614,"sourceBytes":28364,"destBytes":16286,"author":"Gabriel Brangers","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/change-your-password-chromebook.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn26@2020_3/2020/09/05/08-50-11-628_c9dd47830af22981.webp","https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-3-1024x563.png":null,"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-4-1024x334.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn80@2020_1/2020/09/05/08-50-14-470_ba5098848a2d010a.webp","https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-5-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn37@2020_1/2020/09/05/08-50-15-769_973b89828a035e0a.webp","https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-6.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn60@2020_6/2020/09/05/08-50-14-649_94107f467bfce407.webp","https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-1024x555.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn52@2020_5/2020/09/05/08-50-14-686_bd5d53f39041c1c7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295810955},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:10","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:10","title":"Surprise! data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/chrome-os-management-print-jobs-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>Yesterday, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/whats-new-with-chrome-os-85-wi-fi-sync-play-pause-video-and-more/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25186\" target=\"_blank\">Chrome OS 85 started rolling out to users right on schedule</a> and with it, there were a number of updates that will make the user experience even more enjoyable. As we had hoped, there are some unannounced features that came along for the ride and one of them blind-sided me this morning. Developers have been <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/printing-scanning-management-app-chromebook/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"15936\" target=\"_blank\">working on print management for Chrome OS</a> off and on over the past few months but I didn&#8217;t think that the feature was anywhere near ready for primetime. <strong>I was wrong. </strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>As one of our <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/patreon-community-launch-chrome-unboxed\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25162\" target=\"_blank\">fellow Chromies pointed out in our Discord chat</a>, Chrome OS 85 added a new app to the launcher called &#8220;Print Jobs.&#8221; Originally branded &#8220;print management app,&#8221; the new feature appears to be a system web app and was recently updated to Print Jobs last month. As you&#8217;d expect, this app will give you a hub for viewing active and historical print jobs. There&#8217;s not a lot going on here at the moment but it does show active and past print jobs. During an active printing session, I was able to cancel the print job which is exactly what you&#8217;d expect this app to do. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25223\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/surprise-chrome-os-85-brings-print-jobs-management-app/screenshot-2020-09-02-at-12-13-02-pm/\" weren&#8217;t expecting to see a print management app in this update but it looks like developers were ready to get this one out the door. This builds on the ongoing updates to Chrome OS&#8217; ability to print with ease. Chromebooks are gaining network access to a wide number of printer types through this evolving process and Print Jobs is a small, albeit important piece to that puzzle. This will be a welcome change for long-time Chromebook users who were once cursed with the inability to install whatever printer they wanted. It will also be a necessary update when Cloud printing finally gets<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/google-cloud-print-shut-down-december-2020/\" target=\"_blank\"> laid to rest in December of 2020</a>. In related news, Chrome OS Canary now lists a &#8220;scanning&#8221; app that should, eventually, allow users to scan directly from their devices without the need to install an app or <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebook-how-to-scan-with-hp-all-in-one-printers/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"2822\" target=\"_blank\">navigate to a web address like you can with HP and other printers.</a>  If you haven&#8217;t discovered the Print Jobs app yet, make sure you&#8217;ve updated to Chrome OS 85 and search the app launcher for &#8220;print jobs.&#8221; I&#8217;m excited to see what other features may be added to this system app in the future. It has definitely been a long time coming. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"newsletterSignupBlock\">\n\tGet Alerted About New Posts On <br class=\"forMobileOnly\"><span class=\"highlighter\">Your Fitbit, it looks like some of the effects are already being realized with Fitbit&#8217;s latest announcement of 2 new watches for 2020 that will feature the Google Assistant baked right in: <strong>The Fitbit Versa 3 and the new Fitbit Sense.</strong>  Both watches are currently up for pre-order already and, according to Fitbit&#8217;s website, both watches will begin shipping on September 25th.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>While there will be reasons to look at the latest Fitbit Versa 3 or choose the upgraded flagship in the Fitbit Sense, we&#8217;re really here to talk about the fact that both of these new wearables will feature the option to utilize the Google Assistant out of the box.  As a Google user and an Assistant user, I leave the Alexa functionality on my Fitbit 2 turned off completely.  There are times where I could see some serious upside to having quick access to voice-enabled functions on my wrist, but not enough to wade into the Amazon waters of virtual assistants when I don&#8217;t really do much at all in Amazon&#8217;s current ecosystem.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>With this new option of Google Assistant at the ready on my wrist, I&#8217;m far more compelled to actually seek out virtual help from a smartwatch for more than just replies to text and instant messages.  Being able to queue up direction in Google Maps, check the weather, set reminders, create calendar events, set timers, set alarms, etc. will all become normal fare for me if I have a watch that uses the Assistant.  <strong>And before you say it, yes I know there are a myriad of WearOS watches out there</strong> that have access to the Assistant, but I&#8217;ve known too many friends who have tried and hated their WearOS watches to ever really consider buying one for myself.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed-youtube aligncenter wp-block-embed is-type-video is-provider-youtube wp-embed-aspect-16-9 wp-has-aspect-ratio\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\n<iframe title=\"A New Era of Innovation: Fitbit Sense\" width=\"500\" height=\"281\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/lJg1-lPmxMI?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; As the versions have progressed, Fitbit just keeps getting better at design and their watches keep adding useful features that users actually need and want.  <strong>With the Versa 3 we get the addition of GPS in the watch and with the Fitbit Sense, we&#8217;re getting a ton of new, handy features like an ECG monitor, skin temp sensor, and a speaker for taking/making calls right on your wrist.</strong>  The Versa 3 will come in at $229.95 and the Sense will run $329.95.  Both are up for pre-order right now.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>While the regulatory steps still need to be cleared for Fitbit to become an official Google company, it will be great to have a direct path to the Google Assistant inside an already-great smartwatch experience while we await news of the deal actually going through.  For users like myself, the Fitbit Versa 2 has been a fantastic companion device that does all the basic things I really need in a smartwatch.  From the looks of these newer models, the Fitbit Versa 3 and Fitbit Sense will simply take that winning formula, add on a few niceties, and bring Google a tad bit more into the https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/hpusistylus-300x169.jpg 300w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/hpusistylus-768x432.jpg 768w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/hpusistylus-1536x864.jpg 1536w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/hpusistylus.jpg 1600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" data-attachment-id=\"17684\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/hps-rechargeable-usi-stylus-is-finally-available-for-purchase/hpusistylus/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/hpusistylus.jpg\" data-orig-size=\"1600,900\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"hpusistylus\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/hpusistylus-300x169.jpg\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/hpusistylus-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/the-chrome-cast-77-an-exclusive-interview-with-usi-chairman-peter-mueller/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25299\" target=\"_blank\">After our conversation today with USI Chairman Peter Mueller over on The Chrome Cast,</a> there&#8217;s a part of the USI (universal stylus initiative) narrative that has been clarified for me that is quite exciting and I&#8217;m so glad to be able to share a bit more detail.  To this point, the only USI pens we&#8217;ve seen are full-sized pens that are meant to live as outer extensions to the Chromebook experience.  While pens like these are great to hold, they aren&#8217;t always the most practical to keep around.  After all, the best pen is the one you have on you at the time, and internally-stowed pens are the ones that find themselves ready for use at a moment&#8217;s notice.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>I&#8217;ve made this argument often and while I&#8217;ve appreciated the growing number of Chromebooks that support the USI standard, the fact that this means you have to figure out a storage solution for that supported pen means that the times I need my pen, I usually don&#8217;t have it close by.  I&#8217;m not an artist or a person who loves handwriting, so my pen is only useful for tasks like signing documents or marking up notes on an image or draft of a document.  The cases for me to get my pen out are not that numerous, so most times I keep the pen in my bag and when the time comes where I might use it, it isn&#8217;t always within reach.  <strong>This is why I love a stowed stylus option.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>And this is precisely why I asked Peter about this &#8216;issue&#8217; during our conversation today.  Worried that USI pens would always be the larger, free-floating pens we&#8217;ve seen thus far, I was dubious that such a pen solution would ever make sense for users like me.  <strong>Thankfully, that isn&#8217;t the case.</strong>  According to Pete, with USI, the protocol is light enough and power-efficient enough that we should begin seeing Chromebooks with internally-stowed pens in the next generation of devices.  While the USI standard does need a bit of power to do all of its magic, a rechargeable pen can get juice when stored inside the Chromebook and always be ready for use when the user needs it.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Apart from our conversation today, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-chromebook-zork-usi-stylus-pen-internal-charge/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"19809\" target=\"_blank\">we&#8217;ve previously found commits pointing to stowed stylus support for some AMD &#8216;Zork&#8217; Chromebooks,</a> but nothing pointing to this feature for Chromebooks in the more affordable range.  That has changed, however, and we&#8217;ve now found proof of internal USI pen storage/charging on at least one &#8216;Dedede&#8217; Chromebook derivative in &#8216;Drawcia&#8217; that we just added to <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-upcoming-development-boards-devices-chrome-os/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"18348\" target=\"_blank\">our master list of upcoming Chromebook devices</a> we are tracking.  The commit is pretty straightforward, but you can see it below along with the commit that shows USI pen support for the same baseboard:</p>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p>UPSTREAM: mb/google/dedede/var/drawcia: Add elan USI touchscreen</p><cite><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/third_party/coreboot/+/2384903\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">via the Chromium Gerrit</a></cite></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p>drawcia: enable stylus charging Drawcia has garage stylus, this patch enables stylus charging when stylus present.</p><cite><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2373330\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">via the Chromium Gerrit</a></cite></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>There are two very cool things happening, here.</strong>  <strong>First,</strong> we&#8217;re seeing more support for stowable, rechargeable USI pens.  Pens that have a recharge method and can be kept safe inside a Chromebook are the right option in my opinion.  Users can always opt to buy an additional, larger USI pen if they want one, but having the built-in stylus always at the ready is obviously a nice touch.  <strong>Second,</strong> we&#8217;re not just seeing this in a flagship device.  &#8216;Dedede&#8217; Chromebooks like &#8216;Drawcia&#8217; will be small-core Intel devices that generally come in at lower prices, so <strong>you can count on internal pens becoming more normalized for even the most affordable Chromebooks once these begin showing up.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>For me, this development and the<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/usi-stylus-pen-chromebook-hands-on\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25054\" target=\"_blank\"> ease of use we&#8217;ve seen in the first working USI pen we have in the office</a> combine to make me all-in on USI pens for Chromebooks and any other device that begins using them.  Standards are good in many cases, and I&#8217;d argue that a standard pen for electronics is one of those spaces.  I love &#8211; LOVE &#8211; the idea that one day down the road I may be able to pick up my USI pen and begin writing or navigating on any device I have in front of me.  Chromebook, Windows laptop, Android phone/tablet?  Sure.  <strong>One day it will all just work, and I&#8217;m very much looking forward to that.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<img src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/patreonInContentDesktop.jpg\" class=\"patreonDesktop\">\n\n\n\n<div class=\"newsletterSignupBlock\">\n\tGet Alerted About New Posts On <br data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/t-mobile-project-10-million-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>The Un-Carrier has been busy as of late. On the heels of the company finalizing its merger with Sprint, T-Mobile has been working steadily to expand 5G coverage and get high-speed internet into the hands of as many customers as possible. T-Mobile recently announced a three-part initiative that consists of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.t-mobile.com/business/government/first-responders-connecting-heroes\" target=\"_blank\">free service to America&#8217;s First Responders</a> and the T-Mobile Connect plan that offers unlimited talk and text and 2GB of data for as little as $15/month. <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://prepaid.t-mobile.com/prepaid-plans/connect\" target=\"_blank\">T-Mobile Connect</a> also adds an extra 500MB of data each year for up to five years at no additional cost. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>The third and final phase of this initiative comes in the form of a 10 billion dollar commitment to our country&#8217;s education systems. Project 10 Million will span five years and will provide eligible school districts access to free internet for underserved students. This will come in the form of a free mobile hotspot and 100GB of yearly data at no cost to eligible families. </p>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p>Education is the great leveler, but without internet access, kids will be left behind. T-Mobile has a big goal – to deliver connectivity to every child who needs it across the U.S. Starting now with our historic Project 10Million commitment, we’re going to help open A LOT of doors to opportunity that might have previously been closed</p><cite><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.t-mobile.com/news/community/tmobile-launches-project-10million-initiative\" target=\"_blank\">T-Mobile</a><a href=\"https://www.t-mobile.com/news/community/tmobile-launches-project-10million-initiative\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"> CEO Mike Sievert</a></cite></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<p>In addition to free internet, T-Mobile is working to make is easier for students to get access to devices. Project 10 Million will soon provide eligible students with tablets, PCs and Chromebooks at-cost to ensure a viable solution for at-home learning. Among these devices are the Samsung Chromebook 4 and the Lenovo 100e Chromebook. Participants in the project can get up to 5 devices at cost per eligible line. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>At-cost devices</h2>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>Coolpad Tasker tablet</li><li>Samsung Chromebook 4</li><li>Lenovo 100e Chromebook (Coming soon)</li><li>Lenovo 100e Windows PC (Coming soon)</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>To find out if your school has joined Project 10 Million, contact your school administrator. If you&#8217;d like to see your district join, you can contact your administration and ask them to sign up <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.t-mobile.com/business/education/project-10-million?cmpid=TFB_RAD_P_20TENMM_OU0ZJSRRLLM0FYL758187\" target=\"_blank\">here</a>.
