href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-geforce-now-web-player-exclusive-important\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"24901\" target=\"_blank\">even as we sing the praises of GeForce NOW on Chromebooks,</a> <strong>Stadia did it all first.</strong>  Sure, the two platforms take quite different approaches to the game streaming industry, but they both do things quite well.  One of Stadia&#8217;s biggest draws right now is the fact that Google continues to go above and beyond in offering free games to Pro subscribers.  Initially promising only one or two titles a month, we&#8217;ve routinely seen months with 4-6 new titles added to play for free for users in the Pro tier.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This month is no different as Stadia has given Pro subscribers an additional six games to begin playing for free, taking the grand total of free Pro games up over 30 since Stadia&#8217;s launch.  Along with these new titles, 3 free Pro games will drop from the list of games you can claim for free on August 31st, so make sure and go snag them while you can.  Those titles include <strong><em>Get Packed, Kona, and GRID.</em></strong>  For the new games being added, <a href=\"https://community.stadia.com/t5/Stadia-Community-Blog/This-Week-on-Stadia-Six-more-free-games-headed-to-Pro-in/ba-p/28703\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">here&#8217;s what Stadia has to say about each:</a></p>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p><strong>Bomberman R Online:</strong> ake on 63 other players in Super Bomberman R Online! It’s the biggest Bomberman challenge ever. <strong>(First on Stadia)</strong></p><p><strong>Gunsport:</strong> Gunsport is an action-packed two-on-two competitive challenge. Take on rival teams in a rapid-fire trick-shot competition on Stadia Pro. <strong>(First on Stadia)</strong></p><p><strong>Hitman:</strong> Hide in plain sight in Hitman, the stylish stealth action game where you use disguise and your wits to infiltrate fantastic international locales.</p><p><strong>Hello Neighbor:</strong> Something strange and sinister is going on down the street in Hello Neighbor. You can play it free with Stadia Pro starting September 1. Since Embr is still in Early Access, the developers are continuing to add to the game to give you the best experience.</p></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<p>As Stadia&#8217;s library continues to grow with existing games many players already know and love and Stadia firsts like Bomberman R Online and Gunsport, Google keeps making the platform more and more attractive to new players.  As we&#8217;ve watched the development of game streaming happen over the past year, one thing is certain: <strong>this is a long play.</strong>  More games and better experiences will draw more players over time.  Once all three are in place, Stadia will thrive, but it will take time.  If Google keeps throwing free stuff at subscribers like this, its definitely another step in the right direction.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"BuyButton\" the Universal Stylus Initiative and what it means for the future of buying a pen for your Chromebook. The concept is a brilliant one. Create a universal standard for digital pens so when you purchase one, it works on a range of devices with the same functionality and reliability. The biggest obstacle we&#8217;ve seen with the emerging tech is availability. More and more Chromebooks are hitting the market with the USI compatibility on board but the pens are nowhere to be found. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>HP <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/hps-rechargeable-usi-stylus-is-finally-available-for-purchase/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"17682\" target=\"_blank\">quietly released its rechargeable USI stylus</a> but it has since sold out and the only place you can find it is on Amazon at an inflated cost. ASUS and Lenovo both have pens on the way and you can even find listings for them but they simply haven&#8217;t hit the supply channels yet. Thankfully, there are some third-party companies that are and will be creating &#8220;universal&#8221; styluses and one such company has one available to ship within the next week and a half. iPlume&#8217;s USI pen is powered by a AAAA battery and features two barrel buttons. It happens to be identical to a couple of devices we have in the office. We&#8217;re still taking some time to do a full review but I can say that they work perfectly with devices such as the Lenovo Chromebook Duet, Chromebook 10e and the Acer Chromebook Spin 713. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>The iPlume listing popped up a few days back but quickly sold out and the listing was marked as such. Now, you can order the stylus once again for $49 and shipping is slated to start September 8. If you are shopping for a USI stylus, this and the HP are the only two that we are aware of at the moment that are actually available. If you decide to check out other &#8220;universal&#8221; styluses, make sure you see the USI logo somewhere so you can be sure it is legit. week ago,</a> I honestly thought it was as simple as NVIDIA deciding to launch a web-based player similar to Stadia&#8217;s version of the same thing.  After all, Stadia&#8217;s been at it for a solid 9 months at this point, so NVIDIA likely learned a thing or two about pushing game streaming services through web-based technologies from Stadia&#8217;s ups and downs.  Never mind the fact that much of the plumbing needed to make low-latency game streaming possible on the web is done in Chrome via open source standards for the Chromium projects.  <strong>All that work isn&#8217;t just for Stadia and can be easily leveraged by others like NVIDIA when needed.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Stadia&#8217;s web player isn&#8217;t without faults and to test that assertion, I launched into PUBG right before writing this article and still have tons of odd mouse movement jitter and a recurring issue where holding the &#8216;W&#8217; key to move forward simply stops working.  When running from the dangerous, oncoming blue, it&#8217;s really a bummer when your character just stops all of the sudden.  Don&#8217;t get me wrong, the web portal for Stadia is still wildly impressive, <strong>but it isn&#8217;t without flaw.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/nvidia-geforce-now-chromebook-suppport-web-player-stadia-trouble/\" target=\"_blank\">When NVIDIA announced their take on their own web-based player,</a> I simply thought they&#8217;d base it in Chrome and make it available wherever Chrome lives.  While not necessary for the big two desktop platforms (Windows and MacOS have dedicated GeForce NOW apps, after all), I honestly thought the Chrome browser would be the primary factor involved in making GeForce NOW a reality on the web.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>What I didn&#8217;t realize at the onset of the service is the fact that <strong>NVIDIA chose to launch the GeForce NOW web experience for Chromebooks.  Period.</strong>  This isn&#8217;t a <em>Chrome-specific ability.</em>  Instead, this is a <em>Chrome OS-specific ability.</em>  And, honestly, that was exciting for us to learn.  You have to understand that as a Chromebook user and unabashed Chrome OS fan/nerd, I constantly &#8211; CONSTANTLY &#8211; deal with platform limitations when it comes to app support.  Believe it or not, many popular applications have either useless Android versions or don&#8217;t bother with web apps of any sort (please sense my sarcasm, here).  Though they could easily leverage either platform, they simply don&#8217;t, and that means Chromebook users are left out in the cold for a lot of things.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>I&#8217;m used to this reality by now and many other users are as well, but I can&#8217;t lie: <strong>when a big company chooses to target Chromebook users as a primary audience and makes a product for Chrome OS and for Chrome OS alone, I get a little giddy inside.</strong>  We Chromebook users don&#8217;t get a ton of stuff that is just for us, and when it happens I still find myself a bit dubious about the whole thing.  I honestly had trouble believing NVIDIA launched an entire web experience for GeForce NOW just for Chromebooks when they first announced it, but that is exactly what they have done.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"crp_related crp_related_block  \"><h5>more from Chrome Unboxed</h5><ul><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/nvidia-geforce-now-games-studios-cyberpunk-2077-million-users/\"    target=\"_blank\"  class=\"post-15434\"><img loading=\"lazy\"  width=\"150\" height=\"150\"  src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/02/NVIDIAgeforceNowChromebookAndroid-150x150.jpg\" class=\"crp_thumb crp_featured\" alt=\"NVIDIA GeForce NOW loses some games but still gaining momentum\" title=\"NVIDIA GeForce NOW loses some games but still gaining momentum\" /><span class=\"crp_title\">NVIDIA GeForce NOW loses some games but still gaining momentum</span></a><span class=\"crp_author\">  by <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/author/robbypayne/\">Robby Payne</a></span> </li></ul><div class=\"crp_clear\"></div></div>\n\n\n<h2>Why it matters</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>This all becomes important in two big ways.  <strong>On one hand, we now have a web-based game streaming experience that is flat-out fantastic on Chromebooks.</strong>  While I&#8217;ve played Stadia here and there on the web when I don&#8217;t have a TV/Chromecast handy, I&#8217;m drawn to GeForce NOW on the web as a stable, usable, and highly-playable platform for games like Fortnite, APEX Legends, and Hyper Scape.  <strong>It&#8217;s not just a novelty:</strong> it is supremely playable and so much fun that I honestly forget I&#8217;m streaming games from a server most times.  I don&#8217;t know this for fact, but I&#8217;d say part of that great experience is the fact that NVIDIA only focused on one version of Chrome for the experience instead of having to figure out all the issues that may arise on Windows and MacOS, too.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>On the other hand, the arguably more-important factor here is that a company the size of NVIDIA <em>sees</em> Chrome OS.  <em>Really sees it.</em></strong>  While Chromebooks haven&#8217;t historically been a legitimate development target, it seems that period may be coming to an end.  Instead of being the last group software makers consider, perhaps the recent growth and adoption of Chrome OS is finally starting to make the case that Chromebook users aren&#8217;t second-class citizens and are worth considering when building experiences.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Take Adobe Premiere Rush as an example.  When the app launched on more-popular operating systems over a year ago, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/adobe-premier-rush-android-chromebook-chrome-os/\" target=\"_blank\">Chromebook support was promised.</a>  Over a year later, we still have little proof that the app is actually going to ship any time soon.  <strong>Why is that? </strong> Adobe clearly doesn&#8217;t see the benefit in engaging Chromebook users with their services or at least didn&#8217;t until recently.  <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/adobe-premiere-rush-chromebooks-chrome-os-play-store\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"24820\">With the app showing up at random for some users</a> in the Play Store on Chrome OS, perhaps that is changing, but it doesn&#8217;t change the fact that Adobe &#8211; like many other software companies &#8211; views Chromebooks as a side project and not worth their full attention.  <strong>Can you imagine Premiere Rush just skipping out on iOS?  Exactly.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>NVIDIA is a massive company and well aware of the potential of different operating systems.  I don&#8217;t think many people would have blamed them if they just shelved the whole GeForce on Chromebooks idea.  <strong>But they didn&#8217;t. </strong> Instead, it seems they have fully leaned in and made something quite special, and that says something about the potential and benefit NVIDIA sees in the Chromebook user community.  As we&#8217;ve said for years, the population of Chromebook users is growing rapidly and those that see this and begin taking advantage of it will reap the benefits of a user base that is thirsty for great software for their hardware.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>The ramifications of this could be quite large, honestly. </strong> If app developers who build web apps, Android apps, or Linux apps begin seeing larger companies like NVIDIA taking Chrome OS very seriously and having success, there&#8217;s a big chance that they will begin to follow suit.  <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/krita-android-chrome-os-chromebooks-free-painting-professional-desktop-app/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"18295\" target=\"_blank\">I&#8217;ve harped on this before</a> and I&#8217;ll say it until I&#8217;m blue in the face: Android has the ability to deliver solid desktop apps if developers choose to make it so.  Thus far, many have chosen not to and I&#8217;d wager they are missing a massive, growing crowd of users that could potentially adopt their app in droves if it was a solid experience on the larger screen of their Chromebook.  </p>\n\n\n\n<p>The same effect could happen with web apps and Linux apps, too.  As developers see the potential that sits in the ever-expanding user base for Chrome OS, perhaps more time, effort, and intentionality will follow.  As a long-time Chromebook user, I know that&#8217;s exactly what I&#8217;m after.  I want great app experiences regardless of where that app comes from.  I want solid options and apps that do awesome things and simply perform on my Chromebook.  Comapanies that see this, develop things like this, and deliver those products to market have a very good chance of earning my loyalty as a user. <strong>And I&#8217;d guarantee I&#8217;m far from the only one who thinks that.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://fave.co/2Sxx7wt\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"BuyButton\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Sign Up for GeForce NOW</a></p>\n\n\n\n<div data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ChromeFullScreenWebCapture-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>As more and more of us find ourselves working and learning remotely, collaboration and teamwork become a tad more difficult.  After all, simple tasks like reviewing a document or design template aren&#8217;t as straight forward as they once were when most of us were in shared workspaces.  Without the ability to just walk over to a coworker&#8217;s desk and point out things that need an adjustment, <strong>the ability to capture media and annotate that media becomes pretty important.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>I&#8217;ve had countless times where I&#8217;ve needed to do something like this, but the thing I needed to annotate has been a website.  Not just the top fold, but the entire homepage or and entire internal page.  For me and many others, the task of getting a single image of the entirety of a website is a bit daunting and time consuming if you don&#8217;t have the right tools at your disposal.  With that in mind, after <a href=\"https://www.aboutchromebooks.com/news/how-to-screen-capture-a-full-webpage-on-a-chromebook/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">seeing a post by About Chromebooks on the same topic,</a> we wanted to offer up a couple ways to achieve this task in cleanest, fastest, simplest way possible.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>The built-in Chrome method</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Highlighted in Kevin&#8217;s piece about this same thing, there is a way to snag a full website screen grab with no extensions or additional tools needed.  The functionality is hidden in the devleoper tools, so it&#8217;s not quite as simplistic as the second method we&#8217;ll highlight, but it is nice that this method will always be there in Chrome regardless of whether or not you&#8217;ve installed an extension prior.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>To get this working, you simply need to open up the developer tools  by keyboard shortcut <strong>(CTRL + SHIFT + I)</strong> or by right-clicking anywhere on the website and selecting &#8216;Inspect&#8217; from the list.  Once there, open up a search by hitting <strong>CTRL + SHIFT + P</strong> and then type the word &#8216;screen&#8217; to see the handful of screenshot options.   Select the one called &#8216;Capture full size screenshot&#8217; and in a few seconds, you&#8217;ll be prompted to save your full screenshot via the Files app.  Easy!</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"24954\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-full-website-screen-capture-extension-developer-tools/developertoolssearch/\" sizes=\"(max-width: 565px) 100vw, 565px\" /><figcaption>searching developer tools for screenshot options</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2>The even-simpler extension method</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>If any of that up there feels like a bit too much work, there is an extension option for this exact same thing that is quite a bit more user-friendly, available in the Chrome Web Store, and comes highly-rated from the more than 4 million users and 45,000 reviews.  We went hands-on with the <a href=\"https://chrome.google.com/webstore/detail/gofullpage-full-page-scre/fdpohaocaechififmbbbbbknoalclacl/related?hl=en\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">GoFullPage extension</a> and, not-surprisingly, it works just as expected.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"crp_related crp_related_block  \"><h5>more from Chrome Unboxed</h5><ul><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/which-chromebook-buying-help-choices-5-questions/\"    target=\"_blank\"  class=\"post-12873\"><img loading=\"lazy\"  width=\"150\" height=\"150\"  src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/chromebook-buying-guide-choice-5-questions-150x150.jpg\" class=\"crp_thumb crp_featured\" alt=\"How to choose the right Chromebook with 5 simple questions [VIDEO]\" title=\"How to choose the right Chromebook with 5 simple questions [VIDEO]\" /><span class=\"crp_title\">How to choose the right Chromebook with 5 simple questions [VIDEO]</span></a><span class=\"crp_author\">  by <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/author/robbypayne/\">Robby Payne</a></span> </li></ul><div class=\"crp_clear\"></div></div>\n\n\n<p>After installing the extension, you get a few options like image format (PNG vs. JPG), some resizing tools, and the ability to set parameters on what to do with the screen grab once it has been captured.  You can download your finished capture as an image or PDF and there is a simple image editor built in as well for adding stickers and basic shapes to your screen capture.  That last feature will cost you a small subscription fee, though, so if you have markup tools you already use, I&#8217;d just stick with those for now.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Overall, this method is by far an easier option for those that need to grab full website screenshots, but I&#8217;d still lean towards using the developer tools method for simplicity&#8217;s sake.  I like to keep my Chrome extensions as minimal as possible, so even though the developer tool method takes a few more steps to memorize, I love the fact that this functionality is simply built right into Chrome already.  I would love to see this just become an option built into the standard screen grab feature, but for now it will remain tucked away as a developer option.  Oh, and in the event that you are wondering about those basic screen capture options, a standard screen grab is performed by a <strong>CTRL + Overview Button</strong> and a re-sizable screen grab can be done with <strong>CTRL + SHIFT + Overview Button.</strong>  Have fun!</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"BuyButton\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Shop Best data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/NewWaveChromebooksEarly2020-1024x711.jpg\" /></a>\n<p id=\"update\"><strong>UPDATE &#8211; 9/4/2020: </strong>Based on the recent finds, we&#8217;re adding quite a few devices to the mix today.  We have some Tiger Lake Chromebooks, some AMD Chromebooks, some new MediaTek 8183 Chromebooks, and some Jasper Lake Chromebooks to add to the ever-expanding list in this update, so take a look!</p>\n\n\n\n<p>From time to time, it is useful to get your thoughts in one place.  As we continue to track new baseboards and upcoming Chrome OS devices on a daily basis, it can become a bit confusing for us as writers and for you as readers exactly which board is expected to do what.  A few years ago, we&#8217;d be tracking a handful of devices, see those devices arrive, and move on to looking for more.  It was pretty easy to keep all the newness in front of us back then, <strong>but it&#8217;s a very different story these days.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Looking at my notes and my starred/saved changes from the Chromium Repositories, there are <strong><em>so many</em></strong> new devices in development across multiple different baseboards with a wide assortment of chip sets, configurations, and form factors.  As I began looking across all those boards and upcoming devices, it hit me that we&#8217;d do well to take some inventory of where we are, where we&#8217;re going, and what all these code-names and baseboards have to do with upcoming Chromebooks.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>A quick note in the event that all this is new to you:</strong> baseboards and overlays are code-named in the open source Chromium Repositories and usually exist these days in a particular structure.  There are unibuild boards that spawn multiple different devices with their own code-named overlays.  These devices will be similar on the inside, but each one could be a different Chromebook made by a different manufacturer.  The recently released Lenovo Flex 5 and ASUS Chromebook C436 are both based on the unibuild &#8216;Hatch&#8217; baseboard, for example, and are quite different on the outside. </p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>There&#8217;s a lot of info to take in here, so this is how we&#8217;ll proceed:</strong> we&#8217;ll put each main, unibuild board as a heading, explain what the main features are of that board, and then list the overlays and devices being built off of that board.  We&#8217;ll link the lists to what we know about these upcoming Chromebooks so you can research further if you&#8217;d like. So, with that in mind, let&#8217;s dive in and see everything we know about at this point in 2020.</p>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Kukui&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>The &#8216;Kukui&#8217; baseboard is the unibuild that has already spawned the Lenovo 10e and the Chromebook Duet.  We know there are more devices coming based on this board with the possibility of at least one more tablet/detachable variant.  These Chromebooks will run on the MediaTek P60T chip set and, like the Duet, will be decent performers with great battery life.</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/unboxing-the-lenovo-chromebook-duet/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Krane&#8217; (Lenovo Chromebook Duet)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/lenovo-chromebook-10e-duet-tablet-preview/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kodama&#8217; (Lenovo Chromebook 10e)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-chromebook-in-the-works-where-are-you-qualcomm/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Jacuzzi&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-chromebooks-four-new-devices-in-the-works/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Damu&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-chromebooks-four-new-devices-in-the-works/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kappa&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-chromebooks-four-new-devices-in-the-works/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kakadu&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-chromebooks-four-new-devices-in-the-works/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Juniper&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Willow&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Burnet&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Esche&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Hatch&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>The &#8216;Hatch&#8217; baseboard is based on the 10th-gen Intel Comet Lake chips and these Chromebooks come with an armada of upgrades over their 8th-gen predecessors.  &#8216;Hatch&#8217;-based Chromebooks will have faster performance, WiFi 6, Bluetooth 5, optional NVMe storage, fingerprint scanners, pen support, and premium build options.  However, &#8216;Hatch&#8217; boards can also spawn devices like the Lenovo Flex 5 Chromebook that bring much of the goodness of the latest-gen hardware and keep the price in check.  An additional feature of these Chromebooks is or will be the inclusion of regular updates until June of 2028.</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/samsung-galaxy-chromebook-review/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kohaku&#8217; (Samsung Galaxy Chromebook)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/asus-chromebook-flip-c436-review/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Helios&#8217; (ASUS Chromebook Flip C436)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/lenovo-flex-5-chromebook-most-important-of-the-year/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Akemi&#8217; (Lenovo Flex 5 Chromebook)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-hatch-kindred-helios-kohaku-intel-powerful-fast-comet-lake/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kindred&#8217;</a> <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/acer-chromebook-712-durable-rugged-education-schools-hands-on/\" target=\"_blank\">(Acer Chromebook 712)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebook-kled-hatch-family-devices/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kled&#8217; </a><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/acer-chromebook-spin-713-review-flagship-affordable/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">(Acer Chromebook Spin 713)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/hp-launches-3-new-10th-gen-intel-chromebook-for-enterprise/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Dratini&#8217; (HP Pro C640 Chromebook)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/hp-launches-3-new-10th-gen-intel-chromebook-for-enterprise/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Dragonair&#8217; (HP Elite C1030 Chromebook)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/integrated-privacy-screens-are-headed-to-chromebooks-later-this-year/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Drallion&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/upcoming-chromebook-jinlon-getting-a-mysterious-feature-weve-not-seen-before/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Jinlon&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mushu-chromebook-discrete-gpu-project-athena/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Mushu&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/stryke-chromebook-10th-gen-comet-lake-intel-hatch-development/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Stryke&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/asus-chromebook-flip-c436-palkia-affordable/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Palkia&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/nightfury-new-samsung-galaxy-chromebook-plus/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Nightfury&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/comet-lake-chromeboxes-are-headed-our-way-hello-puff/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Puff&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Volteer&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>While we still have a long way to go in getting all the upcoming 10th-gen Comet Lake devices out of development and into users&#8217; hands, that doesn&#8217;t mean the Chrome OS developers are just sitting by on the current generation.  Instead, things are continuing to move forward on the latest, greatest chips from Intel in the form of the 11th-gen Tiger Lake 10nm processors.  These devices started development at the end of 2019, so don&#8217;t expect to see anything from this group until the end of 2020 or at shows like CES 2021 next year.</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-begins-prepping-for-intels-10nm-tiger-lake-cpu/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Volteer&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/tiger-lake-chromebook-10nm-deltaur-development/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Deltaur&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/lenovo-chromebook-intel-tiger-lake-11th-gen-malefor/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Malefor&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-10nm-tiger-lake-chromebook-discovered-meet-ripto/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Ripto&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/three-new-tiger-lake-chromebooks-in-the-works-asus-is-in-the-mix/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Mudada&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/three-new-tiger-lake-chromebooks-in-the-works-asus-is-in-the-mix/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Terrador&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/three-new-tiger-lake-chromebooks-in-the-works-asus-is-in-the-mix/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Delbin&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/intel-chromebooks-tiger-lake-new-development-boards/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Voxel&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/intel-chromebooks-tiger-lake-new-development-boards/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Trondo&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/3-new-chromebooks-development-boards-tiger-lake-jasper-lake-intel/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Halvor&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Lingcod&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Lindar&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Todor&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Eldrid&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Asurada&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-5g-soc-premium-chromebook-processor/\" target=\"_blank\">This board, for the time being, stands alone.</a>  Think of &#8216;Asurada&#8217; as a tangent to &#8216;Kukui&#8217; but also as an upgrade.  The chip on board for this one is the MediaTek 8192 and it is a substantial upgrade over the 8183 (also called the Helio P60T) that is found in &#8216;Kukui&#8217; devices.  With the underlying similarities to &#8216;Kukui&#8217;, we expect development to move fast with &#8216;Asurada&#8217; and we&#8217;d expect it to spawn quite a few boards in the coming months.</p>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Zork&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>While we&#8217;ve become accustomed to seeing the latest Intel chips in new Chromebook boards, it is really awesome to see higher-powered AMD chips being worked on for use in a handful of upcoming Chromebooks.  We had a small wave of affordable AMD devices last year, but those were based on the older A4 and A6 chips that offered little in the way of upgrades from the more-affordable mobile Intel processors.  With these new Picasso chips from AMD, Intel may finally have a fight on its hands for top-tier Chromebook performance.  Additionally, there are a couple boards below that are a sort of tandem to &#8216;Zork&#8217; in &#8216;Dalboz&#8217; and &#8216;Ezkinil&#8217; that are swapping the AMD Picasso chips for the newer, more-mobile focused Dali processors.</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebook-zork-takes-amd-to/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Zork&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-mobile-processors-athlon-ryzen-dali-chromebooks/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Trembyle&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-ryzen-picasso-chromebook-morphius-vega-graphics/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Morphius&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-chromebook-picasso-apu-ces-2020/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Mandolin&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-mobile-processors-athlon-ryzen-dali-chromebooks/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Dalboz&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-mobile-processors-athlon-ryzen-dali-chromebooks/\">&#8216;Ezkinil&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-chromebooks-zork-two-new-boards-development/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Vilboz&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-chromebooks-zork-two-new-boards-development/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Berknip&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Dirinboz&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Woomax&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Trogdor&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>This chip set is one we&#8217;ve been looking at for a very, very long time.  &#8216;Trogdor&#8217; is the torch-bearer for what we hope will become the first Qualcomm Snapdragon Chromebook.  In development for years already, we used to keep tabs on &#8216;Cheza&#8217; as the first possible Snapdragon device, but it looks like &#8216;Cheza&#8217; may never materialize as it is based on the Snapdragon 845 chip that is rapidly becoming obsolete.  Instead, &#8216;Trogdor&#8217; looks to leverage the newer Snapdragon Compute 7c chip set that makes far more sense in Chromebooks.  </p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/qualcomm-snapdragon-7c-chromebook/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Trogdor&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-tablet-phone-snapdragon-screen/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Bubs&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/qualcomm-snapdragon-7c-chromebook-development-lazor-trogdor/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Lazor&#8217;</a></li><li>&#8216;<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/?s=cheza\" target=\"_blank\">Cheza</a>&#8216;</li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/pompom-qualcomm-snapdragon-chromebook-production-compal-quanta-coming-soon/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Pompom&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/snapdragon-7c-chromebook-limozeen-trogdor\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25207\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Limozeen&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Dedede&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>We only know a bit about this board, but the main highlight is the Jasper Lake Intel processors that will retain the low price of Intel&#8217;s small core, mobile-focused chips while giving users a very nice speed bump over the current Gemini Lake Chromebooks.  There aren&#8217;t many of these yet, but expect a ton to show up as 2020 rolls on.</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebook-dedede-begins-development-with-rumored-10nm-intel-jasper-lake-processor/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Dedede&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebook-dedede-begins-development-with-rumored-10nm-intel-jasper-lake-processor/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;WaddleDoo&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/3-new-chromebooks-development-boards-tiger-lake-jasper-lake-intel/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;WaddleDee&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/3-new-chromebooks-development-boards-tiger-lake-jasper-lake-intel/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Magolor&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Drawcia&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Boten&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Madoo&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>As time goes by, we&#8217;ll regularly update this post with new boards we find and new news we come across on boards we already have good knowledge about.</strong>  We&#8217;re hopeful this becomes a place you can regularly return to that you may stay up to date on all the Chromebooks on the way.  We thought last year was crazy, but this is already at a whole new level in 2020.  Bookmark this post to stay in the know&#8230;<strong>it&#8217;s going to be a fun ride!</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"BuyButton\" rel=\"noopener While we haven&#8217;t seen anything official about the update going live, Google has announced some new features for Chrome OS. Presumably, these features will be part of the update when it does happen. These updates may seem relatively insignificant in relation to the past few Chrome OS versions but they bring some very useful features to users that&#8217;s what we love to see. We&#8217;ll keep looking for an actual device to update and let you know when it looks like the rollout is live. In the meantime, here&#8217;s what&#8217;s new and headed our way in Chrome OS. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Wi-Fi Sync</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Syncing Wi-Fi passwords across devices may not be the first thing you think of when you&#8217;re logging into a new Chromebook. Most of us are used to uses a device for the first time and setting up the network before logging in. However, with Wi-Fi Sync, you&#8217;ll wish Google had done this years ago. The new feature will sync Wi-Fi credentials to your profile &#8220;keychain&#8221; and carry it to any other device you log into. It may seem like a minor thing but think about all the times you went to your parents&#8217; house and had to get the insanely long password off the back of the router that&#8217;s behind the television where dust bunnies go to die. Yeah, it&#8217;s a pain. Wi-Fi Sync is a brilliant addition to an ecosystem already designed to keep your data synced across devices. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25192\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/whats-new-with-chrome-os-85-wi-fi-sync-play-pause-video-and-more/screenshot_2020-08-31_at_5-09-09_pm-max-1000x1000-1/\" Google</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Simpler, smarter search</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Currently, searching for an item in the Chrome OS settings menu is limited to exact search terms. For example, if I search &#8220;wi-fi&#8221; on Chrome OS 84, I will see any wi-fi-related settings highlighted in yellow. If I change the search term to &#8220;wifi,&#8221; I get nothing. Chrome OS 85 will bring a more intuitive settings search and even give you suggestions for items that may be related to the setting your are seeking. Building on this new feature, future updates will add this search feature to the app launcher. Google states that this is part of the company&#8217;s goal to make the Launcher an &#8220;everything button.&#8221; </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gallery columns-1 is-cropped\"><ul bring more granular controls to your microphone. Users will be able to open the audio settings in the system tray and manually adjust mic levels with a convenient slider. Perfect if your audience is having a little trouble hearing you. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/Microphone_control_1.gif\" alt=\"\"/></figure>\n\n\n<div class=\"crp_related crp_related_block  \"><h5>more from Chrome Unboxed</h5><ul><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/the-best-chromebooks-of-2020-so-far/\"    target=\"_blank\"  class=\"post-19547\"><img loading=\"lazy\"  width=\"150\" height=\"150\"  src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/bestChromebooksOf2020soFar-150x150.jpg\" class=\"crp_thumb crp_featured\" alt=\"The best Chromebooks of 2020 so far [VIDEO]\" title=\"The best Chromebooks of 2020 so far [VIDEO]\" /><span class=\"crp_title\">The best Chromebooks of 2020 so far [VIDEO]</span></a><span class=\"crp_author\">  by <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/author/robbypayne/\">Robby Payne</a></span> </li></ul><div class=\"crp_clear\"></div></div>\n\n\n<h2>Camera tools</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Chrome OS recently changed the default file type the camera to .mp4. This was a much-needed update as this file type is supported by the majority of devices we use on a daily basis. To make the camera even more capable, Chrome OS 85 will add the ability to pause and start video recording so you can create one continuous video file without taking any breaks. You&#8217;ll also be able to capture still images while recording video which is a feature that should be a part of any decent camera.  </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/Untitled__Aug_20_2020_5_21_PM_3.gif\" alt=\"\"/></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>As I said, Chrome OS 85 is scheduled to arrive today. As of the publishing of this article, we haven&#8217;t seen any sign that the server has updated any devices to 85 but we&#8217;ll keep a close watch and update you when it begins to roll out. I&#8217;m anxious to see what other features may come along for the ride. Did you get the update to Chrome OS 85? data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/GoogleNestWifiGamingPreferredMode-1024x682.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>A dependable internet connection is more important now than ever before. With so many of us working or learning from home, it is imperative that we can access coverage in every corner of our home or office. Google&#8217;s Nest Wi-Fi is one of the best solutions around to do just that. The Nest Wi-Fi router is capable of delivering upwards of 600 Mbps to a single device and it will cover up to 2200 sq. ft. href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/3-ways-to-install-linux-packages-on-your-chromebook/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"24997\" target=\"_blank\">we&#8217;ve covered three methods you can use to install Linux packages from the terminal on your Chromebook</a>. Today, we&#8217;re going to look at how to install and use one of the most popular package management tools for Debian/Ubuntu based operating systems. Synaptic Package Manager is a GUI (graphical user interface) for the in-built APT package management system we covered yesterday. Not only does Synaptic provide a visual interface for the installation, upgrading and removal of packages, but it also gives users the ability to add repositories to access additional packages. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>I covered Synaptic Package Manager a few months back. Unfortunately, the updated of the Linux container on Chrome OS to Debian Buster created some dependency issues that prevented it from running properly. After testing our various package managers and software centers, I revisited Synaptic to find it working again with a small tweak or two. <strong>Why would you want to use Synaptic?</strong> Glad you asked. Many Linux users are well-versed in using the terminal to install and run applications and many Linux distros include their own software center for searching and installing packages. You won&#8217;t get that on Linux in Chrome OS. Chromebook users that are interested in exploring new tools and applications via Linux may have little to now experience using command line tools. Synaptic puts a face on the Debian package manager and does a lot of the heavy lifting for the user. You can search for packages, see their descriptions and Synaptic will even show you what dependencies are needed to install a given package. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25033\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/add-synaptic-to-your-chromebook-for-easy-linux-package-management/synaptic-dependencies/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/synaptic-dependencies.png\" data-orig-size=\"1454,1079\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"synaptic-dependencies\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/synaptic-dependencies-300x223.png\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/synaptic-dependencies-1024x760.png\" loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"760\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/synaptic-dependencies-1024x760.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25033\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/synaptic-dependencies-1024x760.png 1024w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/synaptic-dependencies-300x223.png 300w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/synaptic-dependencies-768x570.png 768w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/synaptic-dependencies.png 1454w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><figcaption>Synaptic Package Manager</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>So, let&#8217;s walk through how to install and use Synaptic Package Manager on Chrome OS. First thing&#8217;s first, you&#8217;ll need to get Linux up and running on your device. If this is the first time you&#8217;ve used the Linux container, you can find more information on getting started <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/the-command-line-getting-started-with-linux-apps-on-your-chromebook/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"15431\" target=\"_blank\">here</a>. All set? Great. Let&#8217;s get started. Synaptic is available from the Debian repository so you don&#8217;t have to do any fancy footwork to get it installed. Open up your Linux terminal and type or paste the following command and hit enter. When prompted, hit &#8220;y&#8221; and enter. </p>\n\n\n\n<pre class=\"wp-block-code\"><code>sudo apt install synaptic</code></pre>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Note: </strong><em>If your installation aborts when you hit &#8220;y&#8221; and enter, run the command again but replace <code>apt</code> with <code>apt-get</code> and you should be good to go</em>. </p>\n\n\n<div class=\"crp_related crp_related_block  \"><h5>more from Chrome Unboxed</h5><ul><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/install-synaptic-package-manager-on-you-chromebook/\"    target=\"_blank\"  class=\"post-15582\"><img loading=\"lazy\"  width=\"150\" height=\"150\"  src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/02/synapticmanagerchromeos-150x150.jpg\" class=\"crp_thumb crp_featured\" alt=\"[Update] Install Synaptic Package Manager on your Chromebook\" title=\"[Update] Install Synaptic Package Manager on your Chromebook\" /><span class=\"crp_title\">[Update] Install Synaptic Package Manager on your Chromebook</span></a><span class=\"crp_author\">  by <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/author/gabe/\">Gabriel Brangers</a></span> </li></ul><div class=\"crp_clear\"></div></div>\n\n\n<p>Now, to run Synaptic you should be able to use the <code>synaptic-pkexec</code> in the terminal. Unfortunately, Linux on Chrome OS is running as a virtual machine using the Chromebook as a host. For various reasons, using this command will run Synaptic without any privileges. That means you won&#8217;t be able to use Synaptic to install or upgrade packages and this will render it all but useless. To overcome this, we&#8217;ll run a different command using <code>sudo</code> but first, we have to give the virtual machine access to the host display or the graphic interface won&#8217;t work. To do this we need to run the following command in the terminal.</p>\n\n\n\n<pre class=\"wp-block-code\"><code>xhost +si:localuser:root</code></pre>\n\n\n\n<p>The output for this command should be <code>localuser:root being added to access control list</code>. Now we&#8217;re ready to launch Synaptic. You can do this by running the following command in the terminal. </p>\n\n\n\n<pre class=\"wp-block-code\"><code>sudo synaptic</code></pre>\n\n\n\n<p>Once Synaptic launches, you&#8217;ll be able to find packages by category or you can search by name. Clicking a package won&#8217;t install it automatically, Instead, you will &#8220;mark it for installation&#8221; and you&#8217;ll be prompted to review any necessary dependencies. Once you&#8217;ve mark the packages, simply click &#8220;apply&#8221; and wait for the installation to completer. Since Synaptic is just running &#8220;apt&#8221; commands, you&#8217;ll find your newly installed apps in your app launcher when applicable. To remove a package, just right click an installed package and click &#8220;mark for removal.&#8221; Then, click apply and the package will be removed. Synaptic is a great tool to help you find and install packages while learning your way around the terminal. Next week, we&#8217;ll explore how to add repositories to pull down packages not found in the Buster repository. Stay tuned. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"newsletterSignupBlock\">\n\tGet Alerted About New Posts On <br class=\"forMobileOnly\"><span class=\"highlighter\">Your Schedule</span><br>\n\t<a 16:50:10","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:10","title":"Steam gaming on Chromebooks inches closer as new details on install process emerge","link":"https://chromeunboxed.com/?p=25260","description":"<a data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/steam-games-chrome-os-chromebooks-web-install-app-manager/steamgameschromebookswebinstallappservice/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/SteamGamesChromebooksWebInstallAppService.jpg\" data-orig-size=\"2000,1125\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"SteamGamesChromebooksWebInstallAppService\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/SteamGamesChromebooksWebInstallAppService-300x169.jpg\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/SteamGamesChromebooksWebInstallAppService-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>In 2020, there have been many ways to go about playing Steam-compatible games on Chromebooks.  There have been methods that <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/how-to-install-steam-on-a-chromebook/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"18093\" target=\"_blank\">utilize Linux on Chrome OS</a> in a few different variations and then there&#8217;s the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-geforce-now-web-player-exclusive-important\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"24901\" target=\"_blank\">NVIDIA GeForce NOW approach</a> that recently became available for Chromebook users, but none of those options are what <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/official-steam-support-could-be-headed-to-chromebooks/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"14334\" target=\"_blank\">Kan Liu was speaking of at CES 2020</a> when he made the statement that Steam support for Chrome OS was officially in the works via the Linux container.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Instead, as we&#8217;ve come to find out this summer, <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/borealis-steam-valve-gaming-chromebook-container-half-life-aperture-science/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"19806\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">the path to Steam gaming on Chromebooks will likely take the form of a custom container</a> much like what we&#8217;ll see with <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/parallels-details-emerge-on-how-windows-will-run-on-chrome-os/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"23995\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Parallels and Windows apps on Chromebooks later this year.</a>  It is the same basic method that the Chrome OS team has used to get Linux apps up and running on Chromebooks, but these custom containers can run different operating systems inside and thus, deliver different experiences for users.  For instance, there&#8217;s a ton of work being done on <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-android-11-apps-arcvm-crostini/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">ARCVM, which will be a custom Android container that will bring the Android framework to Chromebooks</a> in a manner far more similar to what we see with Linux apps as opposed to the current ARC++ method we currently have.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>The custom container that the Chrome OS team is building for this Steam experience goes by the name of Borealis</strong> and there are some really fun details that have emerged in the past week from the Chromium Repositories that shed a bit more light on what the Steam experience will be like once it does land on Chrome OS.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>There will be a web-based installer</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>First up, it is becoming clear that there will be a web-based install method for users to get Steam up and running.  This makes sense as the current install method for Steam revolves around <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://store.steampowered.com/about/\" target=\"_blank\">heading to their installer page,</a> choosing your platform, and beginning an install process from there.  From what we&#8217;re seeing in the repositories, <a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2391891\">there will be a web-driven process that will get the entire installer up and running for Chromebooks.</a></p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM.png\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25263\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/steam-games-chrome-os-chromebooks-web-install-app-manager/screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2-25-19-pm/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM.png\" data-orig-size=\"766,1036\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM-222x300.png\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM-757x1024.png\" loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM-757x1024.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25263\" width=\"627\" height=\"848\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM-757x1024.png 757w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM-222x300.png 222w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM.png 766w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 627px) 100vw, 627px\" /></a><figcaption><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2391891\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">via the Chromium Gerrit</a></figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>As you can see in these strings for the web install flow, there is language about <strong>setup, install, completion, VM configurations, errors, and launching.</strong>  Much of this is similar to the flow we see when Linux apps are turned on for a particular Chromebook and that shouldn&#8217;t come as a surprise.  The bigger deal here is the fact that <strong>this install process looks to be originating from a download via a web interface.</strong>  Ideally, users will click the install button, open a file, and the container install and setup will take care of itself.  It is unclear at this time whether or not the native ability to turn on Borealis will be there in the Chrome OS settings like we see with Android apps and Linux apps.  Since they are clearly setting up a web installer to get things going, I&#8217;d wager the answer is no.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Installed games will be handled like all other apps on a Chromebook</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>I&#8217;d argue that this next tidbit is even more impressive than the web installer.  <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2362102/5/components/services/app_service/public/mojom/types.mojom\" target=\"_blank\">From the looks of what we&#8217;re seeing,</a> Steam games you install via the Borealis method will be standalone apps in your app drawer just like any other thing you install on a Chromebook.  This means that launching the game you just installed will be as easy as opening up Chrome or your Files app and these games will even be able to be pinned on your tray.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25267\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/steam-games-chrome-os-chromebooks-web-install-app-manager/screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2-51-05-pm/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.51.05-PM.png\" data-orig-size=\"410,208\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-title=\"Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.51.05-PM\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.51.05-PM-300x152.png\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.51.05-PM.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25267\" href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2362102/5/components/services/app_service/public/mojom/types.mojom\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">via the Chromium Gerrit</a></figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Even better, your games will be a part of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebook-apps-service-android-linux-install-remove-manage/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"7048\" target=\"_blank\">the App Service</a> that wrangles all the installed apps on your Chromebook, meaning you&#8217;ll have the ability to uninstall via a simple right-click or in the larger Apps menu in your settings.  All told, Steam games will look, behave, and feel just like all the other apps you install on your Chromebook and that will make the entire experience of finding, installing, using and removing them fit into the already-defined way of doing things on Chrome OS.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Borealis has a logo</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>If you&#8217;ve noticed, installed Linux apps that don&#8217;t have a proper logo get the generic penguin as a place holder.  As will be the case from time to time, a game will come along and the icon data either won&#8217;t be there or won&#8217;t be correct.  In those cases, Chrome OS needs a fill-in icon to put in its place.  <a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2377770\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Thanks to the commit for this,</a> we have a basic, simple idea of what the logo for the Borealis project looks like.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25266\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/steam-games-chrome-os-chromebooks-web-install-app-manager/borealis/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis.png\" data-orig-size=\"192,192\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"borealis\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis.png\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis.png\" loading=\"lazy\" width=\"192\" height=\"192\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25266\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis.png 192w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis-150x150.png 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 192px) 100vw, 192px\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Simple, but still pretty cool, right?  This will likely stand in as the icon during the download/install process and will show up in your App menu in settings or in your app drawer any time a game doesn&#8217;t come equipped with a properly-oriented icon of its own.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Still work to be done</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>From the looks of the repositories right now, there&#8217;s likely a ton more work to be done before any of this hits open testing phases.  I don&#8217;t have a timeline in mind, but if we see anything before the end of the year, I&#8217;d be shocked.  Granted, a ton of the VM work and plumbing is already in place thanks to the years of work the Chrome OS team has done on the Crostini Project that brings Linux apps to Chromebooks.  Perhaps as this is simply a modified container, the work won&#8217;t be anywhere close to as intense for Borealis as it was for Crostini, <strong>but don&#8217;t expect anything too soon. </strong> </p>\n\n\n\n<p>It&#8217;s encouraging that tests are happening with the web installer and that we&#8217;re already talking about app icons and inclusion in the App Service, but I&#8217;d say we&#8217;re months out at this point from seeing Steam appear on Chromebooks.  When it does, however, <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/google-pixelbook-2-halvor-usb-4-thunderbolt\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25252\">Tiger Lake Chromebooks (like the hopeful Pixelbook 2)</a> and maybe even some <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-ryzen-chromebooks-soon-benchmark-score-increase\" target=\"_blank\">AMD-powered Chromebooks</a> will be around and ready to offer up their far-superior GPUs to users, making for some pretty sweet, local gaming action on Chromebooks.  <strong>Who would have ever thought?</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<img src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/patreonInContentDesktop.jpg\" class=\"patreonDesktop\">\n\n\n\n<div class=\"newsletterSignupBlock\">\n\tGet Alerted About New Posts On <br Buying a Chromebook right now is a mind-searing undertaking. Finding even a decent device for you or your student is near impossible unless you&#8217;re willing to pay hundreds of dollars over retail and you can forget finding a big sale at the moment. Stores like Best Buy can barely keep inventory and Amazon is rife with third-party sellers that have snatched up Chromebooks at retail or on sale and are now charging outlandish prices knowing they can take advantage of desperate shoppers.</p>\n\n\n\n<img src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/patreonInContentDesktop.jpg\" class=\"patreonDesktop\">\n\n\n\n<p>That said, one of the most value-minded devices has just returned to Amazon at its original MSRP and you can grab one if you act very fast. Since its launch, the 13.3&#8243; Flex 5 2-in-1 Chromebook has been a hot item that gets snatched up every time it pops up on Amazon for this price. Over the past few weeks, demand has driven prices for the Flex 5 as high as $700. Thankfully, it appears that Amazon has gotten some back in stock and you can get one while supplies last. They are limited to 2 per order and I&#8217;d bet they&#8217;ll be gone before the end of the day. If you need a great Chromebook and don&#8217;t want to feel like you&#8217;ve been robbed, this is the best thing out there at the moment. It is part of what we all thought would be a new keyboard layout for Chromebooks moving forward after the launch of that device.  Oddly-enough, we didn&#8217;t see this particular layout again until the Pixel Slate a year later and not again until the Pixelbook Go a year after that.  There have been a few variations on the Chrome OS keyboard, like what we saw in <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/dell-latitude-chromebook-enterprise-review-expensive-consumers/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Dell&#8217;s 2019 enterprise-focused, VM-ready Latitude Chromebooks,</a> but there have been no other sightings of the exact top-row layout that the Google devices carry on any other Chromebooks.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>While it is worth noting that the two third-party keyboards that have the Assistant key built in (Logitech K580 and Brydge C-Type) also get this unique top-row layout with the play/pause button added, <strong>no Chromebook has come with it built in except Google&#8217;s own devices. </strong> I went back and looked at videos and images of all the Chromebooks we&#8217;ve reviewed in the past few years and, much to my surprise, there was no other device with this setup.  <strong>Until &#8216;Halvor&#8217;, that is.</strong>  <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2366317/5/board/halvor/board.c\" target=\"_blank\">According to this commit,</a> the layout of the keyboard for &#8216;Halvor&#8217; will match Google&#8217;s own Chromebooks down to the last key.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25067\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/halvor-pixelbook-2-chromebook-made-by-google/screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10-06-04-am/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM.png\" data-orig-size=\"464,352\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM-300x228.png\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM.png\" loading=\"lazy\" width=\"464\" height=\"352\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25067\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM.png 464w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM-300x228.png 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 464px) 100vw, 464px\" /><figcaption><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2366317/5/board/halvor/board.c#67\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">via the Chromium Gerrit</a></figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Is this firm proof that &#8216;Halvor&#8217; is made by Google?  No, just like the addition of the Assistant key isn&#8217;t.</strong>  And as I&#8217;m fully aware of the existence of confirmation bias, I can&#8217;t even completely say that I&#8217;m not falling prey to it right now.  I&#8217;m looking in every nook and cranny for more proof that &#8216;Halvor&#8217; is made by Google not because I want to be right (I obviously do), but because I have a deep, deep desire for Google to show up with a Chromebook for us to love this year.  We&#8217;ll keep digging and we&#8217;re hoping we end up finding a smoking gun, but I&#8217;m also prepared to just be a hopeful Google fan going into October this year.  Who knows, may Stephen Hall over at 9to5 Google will just get this device before then and <a href=\"https://9to5google.com/2019/10/10/exclusive-this-is-google-pixelbook-go-gallery/\">leak it all out like he did with the Pixelbook Go.</a>  <strong>A guy can hope, right?</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"BuyButton\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Shop data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/AMDchromebooksNewFamilyZork-1024x575.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>It&#8217;s no secret that we&#8217;ve been <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-powered-chromebooks-they-may-be-closer-than-you-think/\" target=\"_blank\">waiting an awfully long time for AMD-powered Chromebooks to show up.</a> Sure, we got a little nibble about a year and a half ago when the low-powered, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/hp-chromebook-14-amd-x360-g1/\" target=\"_blank\">cost-effective A4 and A6 devices showed up,</a> but that&#8217;s not what we&#8217;re really after.  We&#8217;re way more excited by the far-more-powerful Ryzen chips that PCs and laptops running Windows get to take advantage of.  AMD&#8217;s lower prices and similar performance are a great fit for Chrome OS when compared to Intel, but <strong>the path has been long as we&#8217;ve waited for these Chromebooks to arrive.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://browser.geekbench.com/v4/cpu/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&#38;q=zork\" target=\"_blank\">I just came across a new benchmark from yesterday (August 31st 2020) over on Geekbench</a> that tells me we may not be waiting much longer for these devices to finally show up.  You see, back when the original benchmarks showed up for the full-powered AMD Chromebooks, <strong>the multi-core scores didn&#8217;t look so hot.</strong> With most of the current-gen Intel Chromebooks like the Acer Chromebook Spin 713, single-core scores are in the 4000-5000 range and the multi-core scores fall in the 13,000-14,000 range.  When the AMD-powered &#8216;Trembyle&#8217; device showed up in April over on Geekbench, the single-core scores checked out, but the multi-core score was a fraction of what we&#8217;d expect from a true Intel competitor at only 7000-8000. <strong> It didn&#8217;t look good.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Fast forward to this latest benchmark, however, and things are looking far, far better.  With a current score of 4059 on single-core and 13303 on multi-core, &#8216;Trembyle&#8217; (based on the &#8216;Zork&#8217; unibuild) looks way more competitive with the current crop of higher-end Chromebooks.  This is more in line with what we expect of the Ryzen 3700C processor that will ship in many of these AMD Chromebooks whenever they do show up.  Keep in mind, these Chromebooks will also come equipped with Radeon Vega Mobile GPU as well, giving them a graphic leg-up on basically anything else on the market until Tiger Lake Chromebooks start showing up later this year and early in 2021 with Intel&#8217;s new Xe integrated GPUs.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>With these increased scores comes an increased expectation that we&#8217;ll begin seeing Chromebooks with AMD chips inside sooner than later.</strong>  It seems the kinks are getting ironed out for these chipsets and perhaps we&#8217;re finally getting closer to seeing what a Chromebook with an AMD processor and GPU can really do.  It is a general trend to see Chromebook benchmarks get better as they approach an actual public launch, so these score increases likely mean we&#8217;re getting much, much closer to seeing a manufacturer announce an AMD-powered Chromebook.  I certainly hope so.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"BuyButton\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Shop Best Chromebooks of 2020 So Far on Chrome At this point, we&#8217;re aware that the service will act as a deeper link between your Chromebook and Android phone by allowing users to share notifications between Chrome OS and Android and also give users the option to continue tasks when moving from phone to Chromebook.  While we&#8217;re not completely sure how it will all work, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebook-android-phone-hub-notifications-integration\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"24505\" target=\"_blank\">it is apparent that the feature is moving along fast</a> and today we have a new addition to the Phone Hub&#8217;s growing arsenal.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.chromestory.com/2020/08/chromebook-ring-phone/\" target=\"_blank\">Found by Chrome Story,</a> a new ability being added to the Phone Hub will allow users to ring their Android phone at full volume if/when it has been misplaced.  As a frequent user of this feature on the Google Assistant side of things (you can ask any Assistant device to do this same task), I&#8217;m excited to see this added to the Phone Hub.  It is worth noting that you can ask the Assistant on your Chromebook to do the same thing right now, but also understood that not everyone uses the Assistant and may still want to have the ability to ring their phone when it is misplaced.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>For those wanting to simply hit a button and find their phone, this will be another great addition to the growing list of valuable functionality that the upcoming Phone Hub will bring to Chromebook users.
